The committee's expenses will be carried by Bai Yunti when he goes north. Bai will go to Shanghai on the evening of the 7th to meet with Kong and discuss. (7th - Special Dispatch)

Tibetan Tusi Telephones Panchen Lama Requesting Him to Enter Tibet to Preside Over the Government

Anqin and Others are Not Representatives of the Tibetan Government

(Nanjing) The Mongolian League received a telegram from Kongsa Tusi of Ganzi, Tibet, stating that since the passing of the Dalai Lama, the Tibetan people have lost their center of gravity and are unable to survive on their own, relying only on the maintenance of the temporary rulers. The Tibetan territory coveted by strong neighbors is particularly worrying. The only need in recent days is to hope that the Panchen Lama will enter Tibet to preside over the government, and will quickly arrive in Tibet to maintain Buddhism and save sentient beings. (7th - Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Tibetan Office in Nanjing issued a statement stating that Anqin and others came to the capital to assist the Panchen Lama in chanting sutras and are not representatives sent by the Tibetan government. (7th - Special Dispatch)

Huang Shaoxiong is Very Busy with Social Engagements in Shanxi

(Taiyuan) Huang Shaoxiong was very busy yesterday and today attending banquets from all sides. He originally planned to visit Sun Dianying in Shanxi, but since Yan Xishan is suffering from cholera in his hometown and needs to go to Suiyuan urgently, he has decided to go to the riverside with He Qian and others tomorrow morning to meet Yan and then go directly to Suiyuan. (7th - Special Dispatch)

Jia Degan Visits Yuan Liang

(Beiping) Jia Degan, accompanied by Han Wen, Counselor Taikman, visited Yuan Liang at the Municipal Government at 10:30 a.m. on the 7th, accompanied by Cai Yuan, and left at 11:00 a.m. Yuan is scheduled to host a banquet for Jia next week. (7th - Central News Agency Dispatch)

Farmers from Xiang Township in Tianjin County Petition to the County Government Again

(Tianjin) More than a thousand farmers, old and young, from the silting area in the north of Tianjin County, went to the County Government again at 2:00 p.m. today to petition for maintaining farmers' livelihoods and not silting the land within the people's fields. The old and young petitioners brought bedding and gathered inside the County Government. They were not persuaded to disperse by the police until 9:00 p.m. and threatened to come again tomorrow. (7th - Special Dispatch)

MGM Films "The Good Earth"

The Script Has Been Revised and Supplemented by the Central Propaganda Department

(Nanjing) A representative sent by MGM Films has come to China to film "The Good Earth." The script has now been revised and supplemented by the Central Propaganda Department, and personnel have been sent to guide the filming of outdoor scenes. (7th - Central News Agency Dispatch)

The Attitude of Kailuan-Tangshan Mine Workers Softens

Some Internal Workers Go Down to Work

The Military Branch Sends Personnel to Tangshan for Investigation

The Japanese Side Indicates that It Has Nothing to Do with Zhao Dazhong

Yu Xuezhong Will Inspect Eastern Hebei

(Tianjin) The attitude of the Kailuan-Tangshan mine workers has softened due to the Provincial Government ordering Zhao Xun and Tao Shangming to suspend mediation and focus on strictly arresting the leaders. There was not much activity on the 7th, but they are still waiting to see if they will resume work. Tao Shangming hinted to local gentry and businessmen to persuade the workers to resume work quickly. Li Yinchun has contacted familiar worker representatives to persuade the workers not to insist anymore. On the 7th, three-tenths of the internal workers in the Tangshan mine went down to work, and the water was extracted from the mine under the supervision of Belgian engineers. The striking workers did not express any opposition. From the evening of the 6th to this morning, Zhao Dazhong has avoided going out except to meet with a few workers and still said that he would not leave Tangshan because of the arrest warrant. Zhao Lei went to Shanhaiguan by night train on the 6th, reportedly for Zhao Dazhong's affairs, seeking protection from the head of a certain country's intelligence agency. The representatives sent by Zhao Dazhong to the Majiagou Linxi Fourth Mine were beaten to a bloody pulp at the Fourth Mine on the 6th and sent back by car with a letter telling Zhao not to daydream that the East Fourth Mine Trade Union would never support a non-mine worker as chairman. (7th - Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Yu Xuezhong plans to inspect eastern Hebei next week, examine the situation in various counties, and conveniently go to the Tangshan Mine. At noon on the 7th, Zhu Shiqin, a section chief of the Beiping Military Branch, was ordered to go to Tangshan to investigate the labor unrest and negotiate with the Japanese side not to protect Zhao Dazhong. It is said that the Japanese side has indicated that it has no relationship with Zhao and has ordered him to leave Tangshan in the next day or two. (7th - Special Dispatch)

Tianjin Public Security Bureau Captures Traitors

(Tianjin) The Tianjin Public Security Bureau captured four traitors in the Sanbuguan area on the 7th who were recruiting workers for the puppet state to go through the passes. Also, the Special First District intercepted traitors between the docks who were recruiting more than 200 workers for the Japanese. (7th - Special Dispatch)

Commentary

The Pessimistic Outlook for the Future of Disarmament

It has been more than ten years since the League of Nations established the Permanent Disarmament Commission in 1920. It has been two years since the official convening of the Disarmament Conference in 1932. During this period, there have been numerous plenary sessions, general committee meetings, subcommittee meetings, and steering committee meetings. The frequency of these meetings is difficult to count. The number of proposals, the intensity of disputes, and the complexity of the agenda are also dizzying and confusing. However, examining the evolution of the past two years and asking what results or achievements have been achieved, one cannot help but feel disappointed.

The most obvious thing is that the results of the previous meetings not only did not lead to any reduction in armaments, but also showed a tendency to re-expand them. We believe that if the great powers participating in the disarmament conference have the sincerity to reduce their armies, they should take Chapter 5 of the Treaty of Versailles, which restricts German armaments, as the basis for discussion. This is because the Allied Powers made a statement in the clauses of this chapter that they would jointly disarm after Germany. When the Allied Powers made this statement, they thought that the only obstacle to peace was Germany. If Germany disarms to the limits allowed by the treaty, there would be no problem with the joint disarmament of all countries. Furthermore, a careful examination of the tone of this statement reveals that it contains the meaning that the disarmament of all countries should take Germany as the standard, and that the real reduction of the armaments of all countries cannot be achieved without this standard.

However, since the opening of the first Disarmament Conference, very few countries have used Chapter 5 of the treaty as the basis for discussion. The great powers all pushed each other around and had other plans. For example, Britain's intention was to focus on reducing land armaments in order to weaken France's hegemonic power in Europe. France knew this, so in addition to using the word "security" as an excuse, it also proposed the organization of an international navy, hinting at its intention to manipulate the British navy as a countermeasure. As for Italy's resonance with Germany, it was purely out of its usual jealousy towards France. Its intention was to divide France's power to strengthen its own position. There was really no country with the sincerity to genuinely disarm. Therefore, Germany was indignant and dissatisfied, and withdrew from the conference on September 14 of this year (1932). The transformation of the Disarmament Conference into an Armament Expansion Conference began at this point. Since the countries were unwilling to reduce their armaments to Germany's level, there was no other way but to allow Germany to slightly reorganize its armaments. After several months of mediation by Britain, the Five-Power Declaration was produced, which transformed the disarmament situation. It allowed Germany to enjoy equal rights under the condition of not endangering the security of other countries. After this declaration, Germany's actions to reorganize its armaments became legal. Extending to March 16 of last year, the British draft made Germany's position to reorganize its armaments stronger. According to this draft, Germany could expand its standing army to 200,000 men within eight years, while France, Italy, Poland and other countries would have to reduce their troops to 200,000 men within eight years. At that time, Britain thought that since it could not make France disarm, it would be better to rearm Germany. Little did they know that the trend of expanding armaments would grow secretly from then on. The facts that have been revealed to people in the past year are like this. Judging from the recent back-and-forth consultations between Britain, France, and Germany in recent months, the trend of expanding armaments has increased unabated. Britain, which previously did not allow Germany to equip small tanks and heavy artillery, also advocated giving them. Germany's demand for a standing army cannot be less than 300,000 men. As for France, it cannot be without suspicion. It seems to contain the intention to overturn the Five-Power Declaration of the previous year. In this complex and contradictory situation, reopening the Disarmament Steering Committee, who would believe that it can have good results?

Looking at the Disarmament Conference in the past two years, we can see that this conference not only has no achievements, but also helps countries expand their armies. The countries that implemented disarmament in the past will now reorganize their armaments. How can the countries with strong armaments today disarm alone and be willing to lag behind? Therefore, Britain's current plan only makes countries compete in armaments and cannot benefit peace in any way. Britain's traditional foreign policy has never wanted a strong power in Europe that is difficult to control. Therefore, before the Russo-Japanese War, Britain once allied with France to contain Russia. After the Russo-Japanese War, it allied with France to contain Germany. Today, France is strong and Germany is weak, so it is better to ally with Germany and Italy. Therefore, its advocacy has always focused on the reduction of land armaments. If France is unwilling to reduce, it may as well allow Germany to increase its armaments slightly, but it is not willing to express it easily. If this is the case, it is difficult to dispel the suspicion of the European countries, and there is really no way to resolve the future of disarmament.

France Clearly States Position, Armament Reduction Reveals a Glimmer of Hope

France First Wants to Understand the Limits of German Armaments

Final Judgment Still Rests with Geneva

Britain Proposes Convening a Conference

To Discuss Treaty Guarantee Issues

(Paris) Today, on the chessboard of European disarmament, France has made another move, namely, the new response to the questions raised by Britain. The statement clarifying France's position has been telegraphed to the French Ambassador to Britain today. The reasons stated by France still seem to protect the interests of the smaller countries in the guarantee agreement, and there is not much progress on the topic of disarmament itself. However, government sources here say that since France has accepted Britain's request to reopen negotiations, there has indeed been progress in the disarmament process. (Sixth National Telegram)

(Paris) Although there are still many apparent difficulties in the Anglo-French negotiations on disarmament and security guarantees, the note proposed by Britain to continue the disarmament and security guarantee conference was delivered to the French government today by the British Ambassador to France, Sir Tyrrell, and has been accepted by the French government. The French Foreign Ministry is also rushing to draft a reply to the British note. France will accept Britain's request in its note and clarify France's position, especially emphasizing the guarantee responsibilities that Britain will bear in the future when [disarmament clauses] are harmed. It is said that France's note can be completed by the end of this week and handed over to Sir Tyrrell. It is widely rumored that the French government will clearly explain in the joint note what kind of guarantees will be welcomed by France. The above news is very important because it can give the dying disarmament conference a glimmer of hope. Previously, the British government had also exhausted all methods to explore France's specific opinions on Britain's initial disarmament memorandum, but in the end, nothing was gained. France's attitude towards a section of Britain's initial disarmament memorandum, namely, the guarantee issue raised when France is attacked by an enemy, is particularly ambiguous. In its note delivered to the British government by Ambassador Corbin, France explained that what France wants to accept is territorial guarantees rather than ordinary guarantees. However, to what extent the future guarantee issue can progress is not something we can know. (Seventh National Telegram)

(London) British Foreign Secretary Simon spent the whole day today studying France's memorandum on disarmament. According to Reuters, the French memorandum proves that Britain's memorandum has made progress. The French memorandum recognizes some changes in the current situation. France previously refused to acknowledge the extent of Germany's existing rearmament, but now it expresses its willingness to discuss Germany's rearmament plans. However, France still insists that the final judgment must rest with the Disarmament Conference. The French memorandum does give people greater hope that a disarmament treaty can be established. At the same time, after a long conversation, French Foreign Minister Barthou told Disarmament Conference Chairman Henderson that the French delegation could support the proposal to convene a general disarmament conference on April 23. Henderson then set off for Geneva to chair the meeting of the Disarmament Conference's core staff on Tuesday. (Seventh Reuters Telegram)

(Paris) It is expected that within a week, the French government will reply to the British government with a memorandum on armaments. It is heard that the document will propose that all paramilitary organizations should be made harmless. The implementation of the treaty must be strictly monitored. Any violation of the treaty must be subject to preliminary economic sanctions. It is expected that Britain and France will make friendly efforts on the latter two conditions, because France does not want the arms treaty to leave any loopholes, while Britain opposes strict restrictions. (Sixth Reuters Telegram)

(Paris) On March 28 of this year, the British government submitted an official document to the French government, raising several questions regarding the guarantees for the implementation of the disarmament treaty mentioned in France's reply on March 17, requesting the French government to explain them. Later, the British government instructed the British Ambassador to France, Sir Tyrrell, to inquire about the French government's opinions on three points: (1) the reduction of France's own armaments, (2) the benefits granted to Germany in the British plan, and (3) guarantees for the implementation of the disarmament treaty. This morning, during the State Council meeting, Foreign Minister Barthou submitted a draft oral note answering the British questions for discussion, which was approved by the State Council. All the questions raised by the British government must be studied in the long term through diplomatic procedures. The oral note is only a brief reply. The content of the note briefly stated that the security issue has always been the focus of French policy. It is gratifying that the British authorities can understand this. However, before accepting the disarmament treaty proposed by the British government, France wants to know how its technical clauses are stipulated. The British side has made some proposals regarding France's own armaments. The French government believes that it must wait until Britain recognizes the military quotas and weapons that must be given to Germany, which are clarified by France, before France can express its own armaments. The oral note also stated that if Germany's rearmament is officially recognized, other countries restricted by the treaty will also request it as an example. As for what methods can be used to protect the future disarmament treaty from being violated, the Foreign Minister will notify the British Foreign Secretary later. As it stands, France cannot recognize Britain's advocacy of allowing Germany to partially rearm while France begins to disarm. (Sixth Havas Telegram)

(Paris) Disarmament Conference Chairman Henderson, accompanied by the Director of the Disarmament Division of the League of Nations, Agnet, visited Foreign Minister Barthou at 10 a.m. The meeting lasted one hour and fifteen minutes. Afterwards, a communique was issued stating that the content of the talks involved the general situation of the Disarmament Conference, and the situation regarding the meeting of the Disarmament Chairman's small committee next Tuesday was discussed in particular. Finally, Barthou assured Henderson that if someone on the small committee proposes to convene a plenary session of the Disarmament Conference on May 23, France will support this proposal. Black Tom Explosion Case in the European War Era

US Will Reopen Old Case

Demanding Compensation from Germany

(Washington) It is now known that the United States intends to ask the Allied Reparations Bureau to re-handle the famous Black Tom explosion case, demanding that Germany compensate 40 million gold yuan. This request is based on the oath of Irish labor activist James Larkin, because Larkin knows a person who is now a senior official in Hitler's administration. This person was the German manager of this case during the European War. Only he knew about the Black Tom explosion case, which caused a loss of 40 million gold yuan and many lives. (Sixth National Telegram)

(New York) In the summer of 1916, 300 trains loaded with ammunition exploded on the Brackton River in Jersey City, killing and injuring hundreds of people. This ammunition was to supply the Allied countries. This matter was done by German spies, intending to cut off the source of ammunition for the Allied countries. It had a great impact on the United States' decision to participate in the war. At that time, the United States demanded 40 million yuan in damages from Germany, but the dispute continued without result. An investigation was conducted at the time of the incident, and an Irishman named Roelken was arrested and imprisoned. After serving his sentence and being released, he was deported in 1922. The train explosion case that had been going on for many years was shelved. Unexpectedly, news has recently been received from Ireland that Roelken, who was deported in 1922, recently detailed to the US Consulate General in Berlin various destructive acts committed by Germans in the United States before the United States entered the war, especially mentioning the ammunition explosion on the Brackton River, and said that a German was involved in the matter, who is now a member of the German government and a close friend of Hitler. He also made the same declaration to a former member of the British military intelligence bureau last December. Washington believes that the US's demand for compensation from Germany for this case has been suspended since 1932. Now that Roelken's declaration has been obtained, this case can be continued. (Sixth Havas Telegram)

France Prepares to Reconcile the Stalemate on War Debts with the US

The Cabinet is Studying Payment Methods

A Big Bomb from Washington Takes Effect Immediately

(Paris) According to well-informed sources today, France may resume paying its war debts to the United States. Several French political leaders said when meeting with a US Associated Press reporter today that the French installment payment of war debts to the US will be due on June 15 of this year. If Prime Minister Dumergue is still in office at that time, the stalemate on war debts may be partially resolved. According to reliable sources from official circles, the members of the French mixed cabinet are currently considering payment methods. There are two proposals for these people: one is to follow the precedent of Britain's credit payment due in June of this year, and the other is to only pay the interest on the war debts due. What the French government urgently wants to know now is whether President Roosevelt is willing to accept France's partial solution to war debts as a guide to clarifying the entire war debt dispute. The French installment payment of war debts to the US due on June 15 of this year totals US$55,845,953, of which US$19,154,047 is interest. The total amount of French war debts to the US is approximately US$4,000,000,000. It is believed that former French Prime Minister Herriot (the French cabinet in the autumn of 1932) in the Dumergue cabinet was the originator of the reconciliation of war debt disputes. Other members of the cabinet are also deeply afraid of the US's anti-France in this turbulent time in Europe, and are thinking of ways to appease the Americans. The French cabinet has not yet discussed the war debt issue, but it is reported that several members of the cabinet have already conducted private research on the possibility of reconciling the war debt stalemate. The French House of Representatives still maintains its previous firm opposition to paying war debts. When the Herriot cabinet insisted on paying the installment payment of war debts due on December 15 of that year in 1932, it resigned due to the opposition of the French House of Representatives. Since the fall of the Herriot cabinet, France has not paid a penny for war debts. What is noteworthy today is that the French cabinet may not consult with the parliament before deciding its attitude towards war debts. Moreover, the French parliament has also granted the Dumergue cabinet the privilege of presiding over financial plans. It is believed that if Mr. Dumergue can be confident that his cabinet is not controlled by the parliament, he can also use this power to plan the source of war debts due in June. Furthermore, there is a very strong group in the French Senate, composed of senators from the French wine-producing regions, whose leader is Rustin. This group agrees that France should take goodwill actions on war debts owed to the US. Teitieu in the Dumergue cabinet is one of the most vehement opponents of paying war debts. Teitieu may express his opinions on the war debt issue in a few days, but a few people expect that Teitieu may change his attitude after listening to the advice of others. (Seventh National Telegram)

Britain's War Debts to the US Not Included in the Budget

(London) It is expected that British Chancellor of the Exchequer Chamberlain will be able to present a publicly welcomed budget on April 17. Well-informed sources in London have learned that the Chancellor will still not include the repayment of war debts owed to the US in the budget, so he can leave sufficient surplus for his disposal. It is expected that Chamberlain will reduce the income tax from five shillings per pound to four shillings and six pence per pound, and will restore the salaries reduced in 1931. It is also hoped that the unemployment benefits previously cut during the financial panic will be restored in the future. Ministry of Finance Seeks to Improve Salt Revenue Inspection Office Administration

Partial Sovereignty to be Recovered

(Nanjing) The Legislative Yuan reviewed the budget of the Ministry of Finance's Salt Revenue Inspection Office and found that the expenditures were excessive and should be reduced accordingly. It is learned that during the second year of the Republic (1913), Yuan Shikai, due to the Second Revolution and the independence of Jiangxi and Nanjing, in order to crush the revolution and consolidate his personal position, disregarded using salt revenue as the first guarantee and customs revenue as the second guarantee to borrow 200 million yuan from foreign banks, stipulating that it be repaid by the fortieth year of the Republic (1951). This loan, because it was signed in Shanghai, was called the Shanghai Loan at the time. Due to the loan relationship, all foreigners were used as inspectors, with particularly high salaries, even reaching 3,000 yuan per month. In recent years, only the coastal, Zhejiang, Huai, and Songjiang areas have remitted salt revenue to the central government, while others, such as Changlu, Sichuan, and Shandong, have been retained and not remitted, causing the first guarantee to become ineffective. It is now being paid from the second guarantee. The current government is determined to rectify the salt administration, gradually improve the administrative aspects of the Inspection Office, and, since the foreign debt is not a mortgage, seek to recover a portion of sovereignty. The number and salaries of foreign inspectors will be revised. (Special Dispatch, 7th)

Achievements of the American Industrial Recovery (New York Correspondence)

A Year in Review: Economy Not Improved, Labor and Management Still Opposed, Future Full of Thorns

New Measures to Reorganize the Blue Eagle Movement

President Roosevelt has just completed one year in office, since taking office last year. What are his achievements during this year? Anyone who pays attention to the current situation in the United States can have a considerable understanding. Even the most sympathetic are still dissatisfied with him. There are about two kinds of criticisms regarding Roosevelt's implementation of industrial recovery—the "Blue Eagle Movement." The first type believes that Roosevelt has indeed made his greatest efforts in the past year. Even if the results were not as expected, if he had not made such efforts, the United States would have been hit even harder by the economic panic. Therefore, considerable satisfaction should be expressed for the industrial recovery. The second type believes that Roosevelt's movement is a runaway train, using a lot of energy but not achieving much. He certainly made his greatest efforts, but the results obtained were too small.

The Blue Eagle Movement has been in effect for eight months now. Although prices rose slightly in September of last year, they fell again by the end of the year. Recently, there has been a tendency to plummet. Not only is it difficult to develop overseas markets temporarily, and Soviet orders are still very limited, but other places are also affected by economic panic. Moreover, there is still no sign of recovery to the prosperity before 1929 in the country. As a result, it has aroused resentment from many parties, especially labor and management. The reasons for the resentment are roughly as follows:

(1) The most fiercely debated and continuous issue is the right of workers to collective bargaining. According to Article 7 of the National Industrial Recovery Act, workers can organize themselves into groups, and the representatives of these groups can be elected by the labor union. They can enter into contracts with capitalists. The same article also guarantees that workers can join labor unions, support labor unions, and organize labor unions. Therefore, workers first organize local labor unions and then form national labor unions, using this strong solidarity to negotiate. On the capitalist side, they naturally dislike this kind of organization, and even do not recognize its existence. For example, US Steel Corporation refused to engage in collective bargaining with the United Mine Workers of America. These kinds of disputes are likely to be prolonged. (2) Shortening working hours, hiring workers, and guaranteeing minimum wages must lead to higher wages, which leads to higher prices. This is exactly the opposite of the spirit of the Blue Eagle Movement.

(3) Capitalists, in order to cover up their losses, always try to make the working capacity tight under the current situation, to produce more products. Therefore, capitalists take the offensive against workers, which is another major cause of disputes.

(4) The situation of workers has not actually improved much. Labor Secretary Perkins once said that by March of this year, only 2.5 million workers had been re-employed. There are at least 10 million unemployed in the United States, or even 15 to 16 million. However, wages increased by 10.6% from June to the end of last year, while the cost of living only increased by 5.4%. This is the result of the Blue Eagle Movement. However, according to the New Republic magazine, from June to December of last year, the personal wage index only increased by 3.7%, while the cost of living index increased by 5.4%. According to this, the result of the Blue Eagle Movement's income and expenditure calculation is that the workers' income is even below the poverty line in June of last year.

Because of this relationship, the American economic revolution, to the implementation of eight months later, re-encounter a new crisis. The people around the President are working hard to turn the current misfortune into future happiness. Therefore, before the 3,500 representatives of more than 600 industrial sectors in the United States, they strongly advocated strengthening the industrial recovery movement. The methods are: (1) The entire industrial sector, under the Blue Eagle cooperation, should raise wages and shorten working hours. (2) Relying solely on government spending cannot relieve unemployment. In the future, the entire industrial sector must work together. (3) Protect the industrial operations of small capital. (4) Maintain the anti-trust law and recognize fair free competition. (5) This kind of social organization transformation must be permanent. (6) Workers have the freedom to elect representatives to make collective contracts with employers. These are the methods to reorganize the Blue Eagle Movement. Whether it can succeed is still questionable. Moreover, the opposition between labor and management is gradually becoming acute. The stimulus of the military industry is only temporary and difficult to develop soundly. The situation in the United States is so shaky and unstable, and how can other parts of the world be any better? (March 4, 1934)

International Business Telegraph

[Special Business Telegraph from Reuters, April 7]

Gold and Silver

London Gold Price Today (7th) The London gold price is 134 shillings and 7 pence, down 6 pence from yesterday.

London Silver Bar Today (7th) The London silver price is 19 pence 9375 for spot and 20 pence for futures, both down 0.625 from yesterday's price. There were few transactions, with India buying in the morning, the United States buying and selling, and China selling.

New York Silver Bar (Today (7th)) The silver market opened quietly and steadily with good sentiment. News came from Washington that senators from the government side might support the passage of the new silver proposal in the middle of next week. This was considered to be within expectations. Later, news came from Washington that the authorities might discuss with the Senate's silver faction to revise the Dies proposal. The market was quiet, and prices were similar to those in London. Apart from the July contract falling by four pounds, the rest rose by six pounds from yesterday.

Bombay Silver Bar The Bombay silver market closed peacefully today (7th), all down three annas. The spot price is 55 rupees.

Exchange Rates

British-American Today (7th) The pound was stronger in the London foreign exchange market, but trading was not active. The British-American exchange rate opened at 5.1625, down 25 from yesterday's closing rate for the US-British exchange rate. At 11 o'clock, it rose by 625 to 5.16875, and at closing, it rose by another 1875 to 5.170625. US$1 is equivalent to 3 shillings and 10 pence 416 British gold.

The New York market price was peaceful, with good sentiment. Merchants made slight purchases.

Japanese Troops Massacre Righteous Army

[Deng Tiemei Still Fighting Japan in the Triangle Area]

Shenyang Correspondence: Commander Deng Tiemei of the Righteous Army has been resisting Japan and saving the country in the Triangle Area since the September 18th Incident. Last winter in December, the Japanese and puppet troops launched a fifth offensive. As of April, they have not yet withdrawn, claiming that they will not withdraw until they have completely cleared the area. The Righteous Army and the Japanese and puppet troops have an average of one encounter every five or six days. According to statistics, the casualties on both sides are over 300. The Righteous Army often uses ambushes to win. Since February, the Japanese army, due to the failure of their offensive, has burned down all the houses in the mountains where the Righteous Army often gathers. Every time they capture officers and soldiers of the Righteous Army, they inflict suffering on them piecemeal, stabbing their bodies all over with knives, then having people slam them into the ground, or placing bombs in their crotches and detonating them, or using vicious dogs to tear them apart, or hitting their heads with stones. All kinds of cruel tortures are unspeakable.

Liu Bandit Flees Back to Shandong Province

Already Reached Xukou, Ju County

Shandong Army Continues to Encircle and Suppress

Jinan Correspondence: The bandit troops of Liu Guitang, after being severely suppressed by General Han, suffering heavy casualties and with only a few hundred remnants left, fled in a sorry state to the border of Jiangsu province. After entering Jiangsu, they actually joined forces with Jiangsu bandits, increasing their numbers to over two thousand. On the evening of the 3rd, they attacked and captured Ganyu County. On the morning of the 4th, they fled southwest to the Shahe Yushan area. In order to exterminate the Liu bandits, the authorities of Jiangsu and Shandong provinces agreed to disregard provincial boundaries and jointly launch a severe suppression campaign to completely eliminate them in one fell swoop. The 22nd Division of the 3rd Route Army of Shandong Province, led by Gu Liangmin, the 20th Division led by Sun Tongxuan, and the cavalry regiment led by Li Xuande, entered Jiangsu in separate routes to pursue and suppress the bandits. Wang Jun, the commander of the 7th Division of the Jiangsu Army, also led heavy troops to deploy in the Dapu Xinpu area. Unexpectedly, just as they were preparing to encircle and suppress, Liu's bandits suddenly fled northeast from Shahe on the night of the 4th, lingering in the area west of Qingkou in southern Ganyu County, hoping to return to Shandong Province. The Shandong troops led by Gu Liangmin and Li Xuande arrived in the Shimenling area south of Ganyu City this morning (5th), where they joined forces with the Jiangsu army to launch an attack, inflicting heavy casualties on the Liu bandits. Since the Liu bandits could not find a foothold in Jiangsu, they took advantage of the Shandong army's return to defense, dividing into two groups. They crossed the Ma Lu Mountain north from northern Jiangsu in the early morning, passed through Heilinzhen and entered Shandong Province, fleeing directly towards the area between Linyi and Ju County. In the morning, they passed through Tangjialou, Sangyuan, Shagou, Guanzhuang, Lijiake, Sanguishan, Zhongyu, Xialing, Bian Mountain, Zhushishan, and other places. At noon, they passed through Xingwangzhuang, Helepo, Dayu'ya, Caogou, Wangjiazhuang, and nearby areas, and then reached Shizilu, still fleeing northwest. In the afternoon, they passed through Youjiagouzi, Guandi, Liangdian, Diaoyutai, Huangjiamiaozi, Fangjialing, Xujialing, Wangjiaguanzhuang. Around 5 p.m., they arrived at Xukou, Xixukou, Baiyashan, and other areas near Dadian, only fifty or sixty li away from Ju County. The two groups of bandits converged in this area, numbering about seven or eight hundred people, and continued to flee. Their goal seemed to be to enter their old nest in Mount Meng.

After receiving the report, provincial governor Han Fuqu ordered Li Xuande to lead his cavalry regiment back to Shandong from Jiangsu to pursue them. He also ordered Sun Tongxuan to lead his troops to advance from northeast of Linyi, intercepting the Liu bandits from the side. He further ordered Xu Wenyao, who had already returned to defense, to lead his troops to Yishui, and Li Xiangchen's troops to proceed to Ju County, to meet and attack the Liu bandits separately. The directly subordinate troops of Gu Liangmin and the groups of Lin Binghai and Kang Zhankui under Ning Chunxiao's command, who had already entered Jiangsu, were also ordered to immediately return to Shandong. Ma Gui's brigade was to move from north of Tancheng back to south of Ju County to jointly encircle and suppress the Liu bandits. All troops were transported by motor vehicles, with the Dadianzhen area as the concentration point. It was estimated that they could reach their destinations separately that night. The Liu bandits were still under heavy military encirclement and suppression, and it was expected that the situation would be resolved soon (5th).

Xuzhou Correspondence: The remnants of the Liu bandits fled south from Ganyu to Shahezhen, where they were attacked by Li Shilong of the 7th Division. They turned northwest and fled back to Huandun on the border of Jiangsu and Shandong. Li's brigade immediately pursued towards Huandun yesterday (5th), and the Shandong army also advanced from the north to encircle and suppress them. Wang Jun believed that the bandits were fleeing in large groups, making bombing effective, but their movements were uncertain and relied on reconnaissance. Therefore, he telegraphed Chairman Chiang the day before yesterday requesting air support. Yesterday, he received Chiang's reply, approving the dispatch of two Corsair aircraft to Xuzhou on the day of Bing, under Wang Jun's command, to fly to the front. According to a telegram received by the military headquarters today, the Liu bandits, numbering two thousand, had fled from Huandun to Jiagushan, Heilinzhen, and other nearby places. Jiagushan and Heilinzhen are located northeast of Huandun, forming a triangular terrain. Li's brigade urgently pursued and attacked, and Wu's group of the Shandong army besieged them, inflicting heavy losses on the bandits. They fled from the Daxushan area and this morning (6th) had fled to the vicinity of Dangshan southeast of Linyi. Li's brigade continued to pursue and had reached between Zhuduji and Chenjialou on the Jiangsu border, vowing to disregard provincial boundaries and assist in the suppression in Shandong. Wang planned to bomb them after the aircraft arrived. According to investigation, Liu Guitang was indeed among the bandits, and he was determined to completely exterminate them. Chen Guofu, chairman of the Jiangsu Provincial Government, telegraphed Xuzhou today, requesting Wang Jun to dispatch a team to Ganyu to maintain order. The military headquarters forwarded the telegram to the front, and Wang had dispatched a team to garrison the area and went to Caopu to supervise the troops. As the bandits fled north, he ordered Brigade Commander Li to advance and attack, and he went to Xin'anzhen today to oversee everything. Regarding the loss and recovery of Ganyu, according to a message received by Commissioner Wang Depu from Donghai Commissioner and a telegram received by County Magistrate Wang Gong from Donghai County Magistrate Kong, the bandits captured the city on the night of the 3rd and retreated on the afternoon of the 4th, staying in the city for half a day. County Magistrate Fu had led the police force to resist, but they were overwhelmed and the police captain was injured. He had now returned to the city to handle the aftermath. The 7th Division's troops could assist in maintaining order upon arrival. However, the bandits kidnapped women everywhere they went, causing great suffering to the people. (6th)

Rumor of the Death in Battle of Bandit Leader Luo Binghui

｜｜Collapse of Pseudo 1359 Military Corps｜｜

Nanchang Correspondence: Military sources report that the main force of the National Army's 4th Division, after occupying Xinqiao in western Fujian last month, was attacked by no less than 30,000 troops from the pseudo 1st Military Corps' 1st and 2nd Divisions, the pseudo 3rd Military Corps' 4th and 5th Divisions, the pseudo 5th Military Corps' 13th Division, and the pseudo 9th Military Corps' 34th Division. Starting from the 25th, they launched alternating attacks day and night. However, the National Army officers and soldiers fought bravely, and by the 26th, the bandits were completely defeated. In this battle, the bandits suffered more than 2,000 casualties, and the losses of pseudo cadres were particularly heavy. There is a rumor that the bandit leader Luo Binghui was killed in action, and fifty or sixty bandit guns were seized. The official side also suffered more than 200 casualties. Recently, the bandit forces have suffered repeated heavy blows, and their morale and supplies are depleted. Therefore, whenever they engage with the National Army, they are routed and easily defeated.

Another report states that the General Headquarters yesterday received a report from Division Commander Pei You, stating that his division conducted a search and suppression operation from the Getengshan Luanni area and encountered the pseudo 28th Army near Hongshiyan. After a fierce battle lasting all day, the bandits were finally defeated and fled towards the Badaohe area that evening. In this battle, hundreds of bandits were killed and many guns were captured. The National Army suffered only a few soldier casualties, etc.

Another report states that Yu Hanmou reported that the entire pseudo 22nd Division, numbering over a thousand, came from Huichang yesterday, intending to attack the Tianxinwei Anti-Communist Corps. He dispatched a certain unit of Li's division to search and suppress them. When they arrived at the Wulongying area, they encountered the bandits. After a fierce battle lasting all day, the officers and soldiers bravely defeated them, killing or wounding over two hundred bandits, capturing over seventy guns, and taking over forty bandit officers and soldiers as prisoners, etc. (April 6th)

Wang and Chiang Discuss the New Life Movement

Wang Calls for Clear Definition of Simplicity

Chiang Advocates Starting with Order and Cleanliness

Nanchang Correspondence: After the New Life Movement Conference held in the capital by party, government, and military circles on the 29th of last month, Wang Zhaoming sent two telegrams to Chairman Chiang one after another, discussing the methods of implementation and the scope to be advocated at present. The telegrams between Wang and Chiang are recorded below: (1) Wang's telegram stated: "[Reading the newspaper, I learned that you are promoting the New Life Movement, which I greatly admire. I have no objection to any of the points, but the point of simplicity seems to need a clear definition. One concern is that excessive interference may turn into harassing the people, and another concern is that those who implement it may be too ostentatious and become hypocritical. For example, last year's National Goods Parade in Beijing actually led to calls to overthrow Western suits, causing great panic among domestic woolen fabric manufacturers, and some advocating for cloth clothing caused great panic in the silk industry. These must be taken into account. I briefly present my views for reference. If you could share the specific methods and content, it would be greatly appreciated for me to respond in Beijing. [Brother] Zhaoming [sealed]", (2) Chiang's reply telegram one, stated, "[Your opinions are highly appreciated. Since the New Life Movement began, the atmosphere has been refreshed, but it is only a preliminary experiment. The items were originally intended to start with the movement of order and the area was intended to start in Nanchang. After it has been effectively implemented and experiences accumulated, it will be extended to other areas. There are too many aspects of our lives that need to be reformed. If everything is done at the same time, it will be too much and neglected, and it will only repeat the past mistakes of slogans and propaganda, or it may be overcorrected and turn into harassing the people. I am also worried about this. I am sending the methods and contents proposed here for your detailed correction. I hope that it can be carefully considered and completed, and then promoted in Beijing to show the national benchmark, which is even more anticipated. Zhongzheng [sealed]", Chiang's reply telegram two, stated, "[Your insightful views are highly admirable. The New Life Movement, in other words, is the improvement of old bad habits. If we want it to be effective, I think it must be from simple to complex, from shallow to deep, public before private, extend to others, from near to far, and from small to large. Therefore, the types of movement may be temporarily limited to order and cleanliness. The steps to take are to set an example, show people a model. All civil servants and students should take the lead in practicing it, advocate for society, emphasize influence rather than coercion, and guide before discipline. Even if discipline must be implemented, it should be limited to civil servants and students, not the common people. The places where discipline is implemented should be limited to institutions, schools, roads, docks, theaters, hotels, and all public places, not private residences. If the people promote it themselves and encourage each other, this belongs to the scope of people's self-governance, which should be implemented by neighborhood associations setting their own rules. The state should not impose mandatory laws, and especially should not be handled by party, government, and military personnel alone, which would lose the people's interest in participating. Moreover, the theory of life is different from the theory of morality. All so-called four no's, six no's, or eight precepts, ten commandments, are mostly personal cultivation and moral issues of mutual encouragement among friends, and should not be mixed into the New Life Movement, which would cause confusion and lose its universal and simple nature, and turn into hypocrisy and decoration. These are my humble opinions. I wonder if they are in line with your views. In addition to sending a separate telegram to the New Life Movement Promotion Association to discuss in detail with the comrades, I also hope to be taught. Zhongzheng Jiang, [sealed]", (April 6th)

Sichuan-Kang (Xikang) Inspection Team Returns East from Chongqing

Both Northern and Southern Groups Arrive in Chongqing Simultaneously

Chongqing Correspondence: The Sichuan-Kang Inspection Team's Southern Group, upon returning to Ya'an in western Sichuan from Xikang, planned to take bamboo rafts down the Ya River the next day. However, due to the raft owner's inability to carry cargo, it was repeatedly delayed. It wasn't until the morning of March 22nd that they left Cangpingshan and boarded the bamboo raft waiting in the Ya River. They untied the cable and traveled southeast, passing through several dangerous rapids and whirlpools. In the evening, they stayed at Luoba Chang, which belongs to Hongya County. At dawn on the 23rd, the bamboo raft continued downstream, passing through Hongya County and reaching Jiajiang County. They went ashore to visit the county government. The county has a population of 170,000 and produces a lot of bamboo. They use young bamboo to make paper, which is quite white. There are many large and small local paper mills, and many families rely on papermaking as a household industry. The trade volume is about two to three million yuan annually. On the 24th, they traveled fifty li by rickshaw from Jiajiang County to Emei County. Because Mount Emei was nearby, they climbed one-third of Mount Emei on the 25th, about forty li, and stayed at Wannian Temple. They went down the mountain on the 26th. In just three days, they only climbed half of Mount Emei. On the 27th, they traveled eighty li from Emei County to Leshan (formerly Jiading Prefecture). The scenery along the way was extremely beautiful, like a painting. The fields were connected horizontally and vertically, resembling the scenery of the Jiangnan region. Recalling the situation on the border between Sichuan and Kang, it was like a wasteland. Leshan is an important town in southwestern Sichuan with flourishing commerce. It covers an area of 9,600 square li, 180 li long and 70 li wide. The whole county has more than 70,000 households, and the city and suburbs have more than 6,000 households, with a total population of 300,000. There are 33 factories. The main trade includes silk production of 4,524,000 taels per year, porcelain production of twenty kilns per year, about 12,000 pieces, white wax production of 54,000 catties per year, and Jialu alkali plant producing 600,000 catties of alkali. The whole county produces 22,400 pieces of thick silk, 8,000 salt tickets, each ticket is 8,000 catties, and 10,290 tons of coal. On the 28th, they stayed in Leshan for a day and went outside the city to visit the Jialu Paper Mill, the Huaxin Silk Mill, and the Jialu Alkali Plant. The scale was small and the production was not much, only meeting the needs of nearby cities and counties. On the 29th, they took a wooden boat from Leshan and went downstream along the upper reaches of the Yangtze River. That day, they stayed in the territory of Qianwei County. On the 30th, they arrived at Niuguan Chang, about forty li from Yibin (Xufu). Because the Sichuan River was dangerous, they could not travel by boat at night and stayed there. On the morning of the 31st, they started the boat downstream and arrived in Yibin at about 8 o'clock. They went to the Yibin branch of the Sichuan River Navigation Administration for a visit. There happened to be an Yizhou ship waiting to depart, so they transferred to that ship immediately. They lifted anchor at noon and stopped in Luzhou that evening. On the evening of April 1st, they arrived in Chongqing, and the members of the Northern Group, Zhang, Chen, and Liu, happened to return east from Chengdu at the same time, arriving in Chongqing at the same time, which was truly a coincidence. After negotiations in Chongqing, it was decided to take the Minsheng Company's Minzhu ship east to Shanghai on the 7th, ending the Sichuan-Kang inspection tour. The materials on the Kang-Tibet issue obtained by the reporter will also be published after boarding the ship.

｜｜Much Secret Planting in Hechao Area｜｜

He previously sent Ma Lanfu, Director of the Department of Civil Affairs, and Cai Bingyan, Director of the Provincial Security Department, to Yingzhou, Shouxian, Haoxian, Guoyang, and other places in northern Anhui, and Hefei, Chaoxian, and other places in central Anhui to investigate whether there was any secret planting. In northern Anhui, due to strict supervision in recent years, there was little planting. However, in the area bordering Hefei, Chaoxian, and Hanshan counties in central Anhui, there was a lot of opium seedling planting, especially in Chaoxian, where it was everywhere. Cai Bingyan, Director of the Security Department, urged the county governments to send teams to supervise the eradication. After receiving the telegram, Wang transferred the First and Third Squadrons under Wuhu County to the Jiang'an River for assembly on the morning of the 1st, led by Deputy Brigade Commander Ren Luyi, and took a special ship to Chaoxian to direct the eradication. If the Red Spear Society still disregarded the law and dared to resist, they should be suppressed and arrested. Hong Ziyuan, the county magistrate of Chaoxian, came to Wuhu yesterday to ask for instructions on this matter and also returned with the team. Currently, the Red Spear Society and ignorant villagers in that county have gathered a large number of people, and the situation seems quite serious. (1st)

Jiangsu Province Stipulates Measures for Unified Management and Control of Fertilizers

Passed and Implemented by the Provincial Government Meeting

Zhenjiang Correspondence: In order to prevent the harms of artificial fertilizers, promote natural fertilizers, and increase agricultural production, the Jiangsu Provincial Government specially stipulated the Jiangsu Province Unified Management and Control of Fertilizers Measures, which was passed by the 646th meeting of the Provincial Government Committee. The measures and explanations are as follows: [Measures, Article 1: The Jiangsu Provincial Government specially stipulates the Jiangsu Province Unified Management and Control of Fertilizers Measures in order to prevent the harms of artificial fertilizers, promote natural fertilizers, and increase agricultural production. Article 2: All kinds of fertilizers imported into Jiangsu Province, whether natural fertilizers or chemical fertilizers, may be subject to unified management and control by the Department of Construction as necessary. Article 3: The Department of Construction shall investigate the needs of farmers at any time and directly or entrust reliable merchants to handle fertilizer operations, but with the principle of promoting the sale of domestic natural fertilizers as a priority, and may prohibit or restrict the free export or import of various fertilizers when necessary, or order the importers to make appropriate matching of various fertilizers. Article 4: All fertilizers that have been designated for unified management and control, except for those operated by the Department of Construction or the entrusted merchants, shall be concentrated at the place of departure by the importer fifteen days before the scheduled departure date, fill out a report form, and submit it to the Department of Construction or its entrusted agency for inspection, together with the marketing certificate and component analysis form issued by the Commodity Inspection Bureau. Only after affixing the approval certificate can it be allowed to depart. Those who have not gone through the aforementioned procedures or are found to have forged or adulterated goods shall be prohibited from importing. The aforementioned report form shall state the place of delivery, and after verification, it shall not be changed at will. After delivery, a certificate shall be obtained from the local government agency and sent to the original approving agency for record. Article 5: All fertilizer stores opened in Jiangsu Province, except for those directly entrusted by the Department of Construction or specially contracted by entrusted merchants, whether wholesale or retail, must go through the following procedures.

Page 8

(1) New operators shall, fifteen days before opening, submit the name of the store, location, total capital, types of fertilizers sold, name of the manager, etc., to the Department of Construction for approval and issuance of a license before they can open. (Fertilizer stores that have already opened before the promulgation of these measures shall complete the above procedures within ten days after the promulgation of these measures). (2) Fertilizer stores that have been licensed to open shall, within ten days after obtaining the license, fill out a report form, stating the types and quantities of fertilizers prepared for sale this year, and submit the registration fee according to the following standards to the Department of Construction for review and registration, and issuance of a registration certificate. Those who have not registered shall not be allowed to operate. A. Natural fertilizers are exempt from registration fees. B. Chemical fertilizers are two jiao per package (each package is 100 kilograms). The aforementioned registration certificate shall be renewed once a year in January. Natural fertilizers that have undergone manufacturing procedures shall be regarded as chemical fertilizers. Article 6: Fertilizer stores shall not sell more fertilizer than their registered amount each year, except for those directly entrusted by the Department of Construction or specially contracted by entrusted merchants. If it is necessary to exceed the amount, they shall first state the reasons and submit them to the Department of Construction for approval and pay double the registration fee. Article 7: The Department of Construction may send personnel to inspect various fertilizer import locations and fertilizer stores at any time. If it is found that there is a violation of the provisions of these measures, a fine of 10% to 90% of the original price of the goods may be imposed, and the goods may be confiscated. Article 8: The agricultural extension stations of each county shall send personnel to various townships at any time to investigate the fertilizer application situation of farmers and report to the Department of Construction for verification. If it is found that there are errors in the application method, they shall immediately guide and correct them. Article 9: Fertilizer stores in this province shall select store clerks to take turns attending training at the Department of Construction. When farmers purchase fertilizers, they shall first inquire about the planting area, soil condition, crop type, and growth status, and sell them accordingly. Article 10: These measures shall be implemented from the date of promulgation by the Jiangsu Provincial Government. (Explanation) (1) After the promulgation of these measures, the Department of Construction shall designate chemical fertilizers for unified management and control first, and entrust the Agricultural Product Marketing Office of the Farmers Bank to handle fertilizer operations. Because the measures stipulate that registration fees and license fees must be paid, except for those operated by the Department of Construction or the entrusted merchants, the procedures are extremely complicated, so in the future, all the original fertilizer stores in this province will have to purchase fertilizers from the Farmers Bank. (2) The fertilizer business of the whole province is concentrated in the Farmers Bank, which is not only easy to manage, but also can obtain considerable income. (3) Previously, the chemical fertilizer stores in each county purchased fertilizers from foreign merchants in Shanghai, and the prices and goods were controlled by them. In the future, when the Farmers Bank purchases fertilizers, it can adopt bidding methods to make the foreign merchants compete with each other or reduce the selling price. (4) At present, the selling price of chemical fertilizers in each county is freely determined by the fertilizer stores, which is extremely inconsistent. Every time the fertilization period arrives, they arbitrarily raise the selling price, which makes the farmers suffer greatly. In the future, it will be uniformly stipulated by the Department of Construction to ensure uniformity]. (5th)

Overview of Japan's Opium Policy in the Northeast

Currently, There are More Than 9 Million Opium Addicts

Annual Consumption Reaches 518.4 Million Yuan

Changchun Correspondence: The Japanese implement an opium monopoly policy in the puppet organization, with the intention of both obtaining economic income and poisoning and destroying our Northeast race, which is a cunning plan and a particularly poisonous heart. The situation is recorded as follows:

Currently, the Japanese have established an Opium Monopoly Bureau in Changchun, and branches have been established in major cities, and distribution offices have been established in various counties. The Bureau has the right to audit the entire territory's opium production, sales, distribution, and punish private sellers. The branches perform the same responsibilities within their designated areas. The rights to financial revenue and expenditure and the punishment of private sellers are all controlled by the Japanese. Currently, there are forty monopoly offices in Jilin, and each office can bring in at least 200 yuan per day, totaling about 8,000 yuan. Changchun has been changed to the puppet capital, and the number of people has greatly increased compared to before, so its opium income is also doubled compared to Jilin city. The opium sold in Liaoning is even more than in Jilin, with daily sales of 10,000 yuan. The sales in the Harbin area are even greater, with a daily income of 16,000 yuan. As for Heilongjiang, Xing'an, and Rehe, because they are located in remote areas, the individual income can be estimated at half of Jilin's, but each place can still earn 4,000 yuan per day, totaling 12,000 yuan for the three places. In total, the above places can sell at least 50,000 yuan of opium per day, which shows that the Japanese blackening policy is difficult to calculate the harm.

Xi Qia, the puppet Minister of Finance, ordered by the Japanese, especially designated opium planting areas in eastern provinces for management. It is estimated that Fengtian designated Changbai, Fusong, Antu, and Linjiang counties, Jilin designated Yanji, Wangqing, Helong, Hunchun, Dongning, Ning'an, Muling, Boli, Mishan, Hulin, Huachuan, Fujin, Tongjiang, Ningqing, Raohe, Fuyuan, Yilan, and other seventeen counties due to suitable soil. The planting in Fengtian and Jilin provinces is mostly adjacent to the Korean border, which the Japanese require for easy protection. Heilongjiang has not designated an area due to its colder geology and unsuitability for planting. Although Rehe has few counties, it is known for its opium production, so it designated Chaoyang, Fuxin, Kailu, Lubei, Tianshan, Lindong, Chifeng, Jianping, Weichang, Lingyuan, Lingnan, Pingyuan, Chengde, Jianping, Fengning, and other sixteen counties. It can be said that the poisoning has spread throughout the Northeast. The number of mu to be planted has not yet been determined.

Since the Japanese implemented the opium poisoning policy for more than two years, the victims have accounted for one-third of the population. According to a survey published by the puppet Ministry of Civil Affairs, opium smokers under the age of fifteen account for 13%, those under the age of twenty-five account for 23%, and those under the age of thirty account for 33%, with a real number of more than 9 million people. Among the 30 million compatriots, one-third of the population has been poisoned by opium. Calculating each person smoking four qian per day, the total amount of opium smoked throughout the year is 12.96 million guan (each guan is 7.5 catties), and each qian is calculated at 4 jiao, totaling 518.4 million yuan. (Northeast News Agency)

Achievements of Foreign Experts of the National Economic Council

Engineering Experts Still Serving in China

Education, Agriculture, and Hygiene Surveys Completed

Silkworm and Political Systems Currently Under Study

The National Economic Council, in order to prepare for the implementation of various construction projects and adapt them to the country's needs, and in accordance with the will of the government, implemented technical cooperation with the League of Nations, hiring League of Nations experts to come to China to conduct various business investigations, research improvements, and development steps, for reference in implementation. The following is an excerpt of the work of each expert in China:

Education

Regarding education, after League of Nations education experts Sandiford, Dr. Donald, Walter H. Henry, and Pinnar arrived in China, they immediately went to Nanjing, Zhenjiang, Wuxi, Suzhou, Shanghai, Hangzhou, Beiping, Tianjin, Guangdong, and other schools to conduct on-the-ground inspections of the implementation of education. After completing the inspections, they gathered in Nanjing, consulted various relevant documents, and began systematic research. They authored a book on the improvement of Chinese education and drafted a preliminary proposal for reforming Chinese education, which was submitted to the National Economic Council for consideration. All of the above experts have left China and returned to Europe.

Engineering

League of Nations Hydraulic Engineering Experts, (1) Pannill, Gowdey, and Sivkin, arrived in China and immediately inspected the Huangpu River port in Wusong and Pudong. They then went to the upper and lower reaches of the Huai River and the North China area for inspections. Each submitted reports on the inspection of water conservancy in the Huai River, North China, and the Shanghai commercial port for reference and adoption by the relevant authorities. They are currently still serving in China. (2) Puddelee is engaged in research on water conservancy work. The results of the research are regularly suggested to the Engineering Department of the National Economic Council. He is still continuing his work. (3) Kaukinky went to Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hunan, and other provinces to survey road routes and construction. The results of the research are regularly suggested to the Highway Department of the National Economic Council for adoption. He is still serving in the Council.

Hygiene

(1) Mechem, assists in planning the preparation and implementation steps of the National Economic Council's hygiene program. Suggestions are regularly submitted to the Central Health Department for adoption. He is still serving in the Council. (2) Cogg, has visited various places along the Yangtze River to investigate the situation regarding the announcement of diseases. Suggestions are regularly submitted for adoption. He has already returned home. (3) Dunbar, has visited various provinces in the north and south to investigate rural hygiene matters. Suggestions are regularly submitted for adoption. He has also returned to Europe.

Agriculture

Tryphonie Berele, has visited Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and North China to conduct on-the-ground inspections of the actual conditions of the rural economy and exchange views with schools in various places. He has already written a preliminary research report on China's agricultural policy and a research report on China's agricultural situation and economic survey. He has now completed his work and returned to Europe.

Silkworm

After League of Nations silkworm expert Mary arrived in China, she personally visited Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Shandong, Sichuan, and other provinces to conduct on-the-ground inspections regarding China's mulberry planting, seed production, silkworm cocoon sales, silk production, and the maintenance of silk factories. She has completed the inspection and has drafted preliminary relief measures. She is still continuing her research in China.

Political Systems

League of Nations political system expert Shen Tao came to China in February of the 22nd year of the Republic, and Mannac came to China in June of the 22nd year of the Republic. The National Economic Council specially compiled various regulations and other application materials for their research. The political system is very important, so Shen and Mannac are currently engaged in research. There are no results yet. Songjiang

The Jiaodiao Bay Police Station Was Destroyed

Wang Jiaxiang, No. 31 Tu in Jiaodiao Bay Township, belonged to a farmer Youfu, who owed several hundred cash to Sun Yuelongjiang, a wind instrument player from Lujiabang. Sun and his old mother went to Zhong's place to collect the debt. Unexpectedly, Sun's mother and Yuelong were insulted and scolded by Zhong, followed by a vicious beating. Sun was unwilling to accept this and reported it to the Jiaodiao Bay Police Station. Zhong did not appear when summoned. Zhong did not repent but instead dared to gather many people and went to the Jiaodiao Bay Police Station to seek revenge. With a crowd of voices, they smashed the doors and windows of the police station. Seeing that he was no match for them, the patrol chief secretly notified the patrol police to notify the Gendarmerie stationed at Yangqiao, No. 31, to rush to the scene to stop them. Two accomplices, Shen Xiuhai and Zhong Xinglin (Youfu's son), were caught on the spot. The patrol police at the station also caught the main offender, Zhong Youfu. They were escorted to the Second Branch Bureau. Wang, the director of the branch bureau, sent patrol chiefs Li Yaokun and Liu Yuming to investigate and verify the facts. Documents were prepared and sent to the Public Security Bureau and then to the Procuratorate for interrogation and handling.

Haimen

Opposition to the Public Burial of Xing Guangshi

Xing Guangshi, a native of this county, devoted more than ten years of his energy to inventing a lightweight textile machine. Unexpectedly, he died of illness before it was completed. His family applied to the National Government for a pension of 10,000 yuan and ordered the county government to allocate 3,000 yuan and 50 mu of public land for Xing's burial. The machine was handed over to the Academia Sinica for continued research. Later, Huang Xijie and others, natives of the county, argued that Xing was from Nantong and was not registered in this county, so he should not be buried by this county. They repeatedly petitioned to stop it. Therefore, the issue of Xing's burial has not yet been resolved.

Resolution of Labor-Management Dispute at Dasheng No. 2 Factory

Dasheng No. 2 Factory has been shut down for half a year, and the workers have suffered greatly. They have repeatedly requested to resume work, but the management stated that the bank group did not approve the loan, making it difficult to resume. In mid-February of this year, it was announced that the factory would be dissolved. The workers expressed their opposition, leading to a dispute. The other day, the Qidong County Government convened representatives from both sides to discuss and mediate, and the following conditions were decided: (1) The Dasheng No. 2 Factory will actively plan to resume work by the board of directors. The date of resuming operations is set for November 1, 23rd year of the Republic. However, if there is a turnaround in the yarn and cloth market before the deadline, the factory should resume operations in advance. If the yarn and cloth market is still sluggish and the financial situation is stagnant by the deadline, the date may be extended as appropriate. (2) When operations are resumed in the future, the old ordinary workers and mechanics, except for the elderly and those incapable of working, should be given priority in employment according to the actual number of people needed in the factory. The factory and the labor union will jointly identify them before the resumption of operations. (3) The severance pay for ordinary workers will be based on two months of the original salary, with each month counted as 30 days. However, the half-month salary borrowed last year will be deducted accordingly. (4) The severance pay for mechanics should be higher than that for ordinary workers, and the severance pay for staff should be higher than that for mechanics. The amount will be discussed separately by both parties. (5) The losses suffered by the workers during the period from the shutdown to the dissolution of the Second Factory will be handled by the labor union after listing the reasons based on the Factory Law and submitting them for explanation and compliance. (6) At the end of the past year, the factory allowed each ordinary worker to be given two dou of corn. It should be reissued within ten days. (7) All severance payments should be paid off within 20 days from the date of mediation. (8) Regarding the labor union's request to issue 7,500 yuan of travel expenses to the workers, the factory representatives should state the suffering of the workers to the board of directors of the Second Factory, and the county government representatives should send a letter to the board of directors, asking them to consider the difficulties of the workers and make efforts to issue the expenses. However, this issue should not affect the above seven articles of the mediation decision. Accompanying mediation items: The Dasheng Hospital and Dasheng Primary School should be maintained by the factory by any means. The above mediation matters were recognized by both parties without objection, and three identical written records were made. Each party's representative signed and sealed them. In addition to the labor-management parties each holding one copy, one copy was kept by the Qidong County Government for record.
