Wuxi to Construct an Airfield

In order to develop private aviation, the Aviation Administration plans to construct an airfield of more than 800 meters square outside the former prefectural cities of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, about ten miles away from the city, and pay attention to the selection of locations that (1) can connect to roads, (2) are easier to drain, and (3) have simple construction. It has been decided that the six counties in Jiangsu Province are: (1) Suzhou, (2) Zhenjiang, (3) Wuxi, (4) Yangzhou, (5) Songjiang, and (6) Wujin.

The Qinfeng Labor Strike is Serious

The female workers in the weaving workshop of Qinfeng Yarn Factory No. 1 Workshop started a strike because the female cloth inspectors were too strict in their inspections and the fines were too harsh. The next day, the two departments of weaving in No. 1 Workshop completely stopped work, and the situation gradually expanded. However, No. 2 Workshop still worked as usual and was not affected at all. However, the factory stated that the cloth evaluation room destroyed the cloth evaluation tables and account books that day, causing serious damage. Fearing other accidents, it specially reported to both the party and government for maintenance. The county government also considered the labor strike to be serious and was concerned that unscrupulous elements might be causing trouble. It immediately discussed with the county party headquarters and specially dispatched the county police brigade to guard the factory. Unexpectedly, this caused a conflict between the female workers and the police team. On the afternoon of the 6th, three to four hundred female workers gathered at the yarn factory industry union on Wanqian Road and formulated four conditions: (1) punish the murderers, (2) release the arrested female worker Bao Afeng, (3) ask the county government to appropriately subsidize the medical expenses of the injured, and (4) the factory will pay the wages for the strike period as usual. After the decision, they were about to petition the party and government agencies, but they were stopped by members sent by the county party headquarters to explain the situation separately. However, some female workers, believing that the police team was still protecting the factory, planned to bring lime bags to the factory to retaliate. The police team, upon hearing the news, immediately strengthened their defenses, closed the factory alley doors, prohibited passage, and prepared fire hydrants for resistance. The situation was extremely serious. The county party headquarters received news beforehand and immediately sent cadre Zhao Xuchang to the factory to inquire about the truth. Wang Wei, the captain of the county police brigade, also personally went to maintain order and arranged everything very closely. Therefore, although there were many female workers, fortunately, no accidents occurred. However, the female workers of No. 2 Workshop were blocked from going to work by the striking female workers holding incense sticks. That night, after nine o'clock, Ye Dezhen, the secretary of the county government, together with Wang, the captain of the police team, and Yao, the director of the trial division, went to the county party headquarters to consult with committee members Gui Wochen and Xu Yongji twice. The factory proposed that the punishment of the murderers should be the premise for starting work, in order to appease the labor side’s demands for increased wages and reduced fines. It was decided that Committee Member Gui would convene representatives of the workers to guide and inquire about the person in charge of causing trouble. As of yesterday (7th) morning, Committee Member Xu of the county party headquarters and Secretary Ye of the county government jointly consulted with the Chamber of Commerce and decided on the principles: (1) The Qinfeng Yarn Factory Labor-Management Dispute Review Committee will hold a meeting immediately for review and approval. (2) The six foremen of the cloth machine room in No. 1 Workshop of the factory will be responsible in writing for ensuring that no other incidents occur in the future, as a guarantee for the factory from now on. The above two items will be negotiated with both the labor and management sides by the party and government. However, the kitchen of No. 2 Workshop (i.e., the new factory) has been completely occupied by the striking female workers, and many important workers in the machine room have also been persuaded to leave, making it impossible to work. The situation still shows signs of expansion.

Changzhou

A Traitor Sets Fire to Tongcheng Yarn Factory

The Tongcheng Yarn Factory, located near Dingyan outside the East Gate of Wu County, was previously leased to Jiuji Company for business. Recently, Jiuji Company ceased operations and was taken back for self-management on March 30. At approximately one o'clock in the morning on the 7th, the bamboo fence on the west side of the factory was torn down. When factory staff and police discovered it and were about to investigate, they suddenly saw that the guardhouse outside the gate of the goods warehouse on the south side and the guardhouse outside the main gate on the east side were on fire. All staff and factory police worked hard to extinguish the fire. Two guardhouses and about three intervals of bamboo fence were burned. Traces of straw and kerosene were found in the guardhouses, indicating that unscrupulous people intentionally set the fire. Fortunately, it was discovered early, preventing it from spreading and causing a major disaster. The incident was reported to the County Government Public Security Bureau for investigation.

Shops Request Rent Reduction

The area west of the main street in Wu County is the most bustling. However, business has plummeted in recent years, and rents are high. In accordance with the precedents set in Shanghai and Suzhou, a tenants' association has been organized to carry out a rent reduction movement. A meeting was held at the Shuonan Public Office on the afternoon of the 7th, and a preparatory meeting was scheduled for the 15th to complete the registration procedures in order to proceed with negotiations.

Yangzhou

Opposite-Sex Companion Trip Almost Caused a Fatal Incident

Slender West Lake outside the North Gate of Yangzhou is crowded with tourists every Spring Festival. This year's Qingming Festival had fine weather, and there were even more tourists. As the sun was setting, by the Great Rainbow Bridge, a beautiful young woman, accompanied by a young man who looked like a worker, was sharing a small boat, talking and laughing freely. Unexpectedly, the woman's father saw them and mistook them for lovers. He angrily ordered the boat to stop. When the woman saw that her father's voice and expression were stern, she was afraid and jumped into the lake. Fortunately, boatman Xiao Yu was agile and pulled her onto the small boat. She was barely breathing. He quickly administered artificial respiration and she thankfully revived. Later, the boatman proved that they had boarded the boat at different times and each paid 500 cash. The woman's father's anger subsided slightly. It was learned that the woman's name was Qiu Xiaozhen and she lived in a small alley behind Guangchumen. The young man's surname was Li, and he was a clerk in a Xu's grocery store in Xu Ningmen. They were strangers to each other. It was inferred that the misunderstanding occurred because they were sharing a boat, almost leading to a fatal incident. It was indeed a close call.

Nanhui

Water Patrol Team Searches County Party Headquarters

Zhu Chunlin, a patrol officer of the Water Patrol Team, led more than ten armed patrolmen to the County Party Headquarters at approximately 11:00 PM last night and searched the office and the bedrooms of the staff. All the staff were awakened from their dreams. When asked for the reason, the patrol officer claimed that he was acting on the instructions of Captain Chen and could not refuse. They had no choice but to allow the search, which resulted in all the documents and equipment in each room being in disarray. Finally, Yuan Geng, a party member dispatched by the Second Directly Subordinate District Branch to the city to collect the preliminary party member forms, was dragged out of bed and arrested. The County Department believed that the Water Patrol Team abused its power, broke into the Party Headquarters late at night and searched arbitrarily, privately arrested party members, acted illegally and recklessly to the extreme. Therefore, they have telegraphed the province for a thorough investigation.

Changshu

Implementation of Tolls for Urban and Rural Telephones

Each rural area in this county is equipped with urban and rural telephones, the expenses of which are borne by each district. The former director of the exchange proposed to charge for telephone calls, which was opposed by local people and stopped. It is now learned that the Construction Department plans to transfer the urban and rural telephones in this county to provincial management, merge them with the provincial long-distance telephone bureau, and implement telephone charges in rural areas. Shan Bao-Ci has been dispatched on the 5th to Changshu to take over. The handover has been completed by Pan Xizu, the director of the exchange in this county. Now, local people here believe that urban and rural telephones were established with local funding, originally to facilitate smooth communication of defense news. Now that tolls are charged, people cannot afford it. Some people have already raised objections.

Ningbo

Bodyguard's Accidental Shot Claims Three Lives

Yan Axing, a farmer from Maoxia, Yushan Township, Yinjiang Bridge, 7th District of Yin County, is 35 years old. He has a mother in her sixties, and his wife, Xu, is 25 years old. She gave birth to a boy just three days ago. Because Axing was on duty this year, he bought meat at the market the day before Qingming (i.e., the 4th) for use. At that time, Zhang, the squad leader of the 3rd District Bodyguard Group stationed at the Yaowang Temple in Zhangcun, led seven armed bodyguards through Maoxia on the highway. Unexpectedly, Axing suddenly turned pale when he saw the armed bodyguards and ran wildly home with the meat. One of the bodyguards, seeing Axing running wildly, suspected that he was not a good person and chased him to his door. He fired a shot from a wooden-cased gun, hitting Axing's vital point. He immediately fell to the ground and died. At the time, Xu was feeding her child in bed. Suddenly hearing the gunshot, she asked what had happened and learned that Axing had been killed. She cried out loudly, and her lower body bled profusely. She died instantly. Axing's mother was caressing Axing's body and crying bitterly. Hearing the sound, she looked back and saw that her daughter-in-law had also died from bleeding. Looking at her newly born grandson, he was also crushed to death by his mother's arm. Four members of the family died instantly, and she was overwhelmed with grief. She went to the city that night and petitioned the Yin County District Court yesterday (the 5th) afternoon at 7:00 PM, requesting justice. Prosecutor Weng opened the court for questioning, comforted her, and ordered her to return. This morning, he went to the village to examine the body in order to handle the case.

The Puxing Steamer Returns Safely

The Puxing Steamer, which travels between Ningbo and Shengshan, was sailing from Yong to Dinghai yesterday (the 3rd) morning and did not stop. It continued south. Chaoyang Steamer caught sight of it and knew it had been robbed. It reported to the Dinghai Puxing Branch, which requested the Water Police Team to send a warship to pursue. The details have been recorded in this newspaper. Yesterday (the 4th) afternoon at 1:00 PM, Puxing Company received two telegrams from Dinghai Puxing Branch: (1) Puxing Steamer arrived in Dinghai at 12:00 PM today and will depart for Yong immediately. The crew is safe. (2) Puxing Steamer arrived in Dinghai and was indeed robbed. The people and the ship are safe. The loss, including the passengers', is worth 2,000 gold. In the evening at 7:00 PM, the company received a long-distance telephone report from the Shenjiamen Branch that Puxing was staying overnight in Shen and would depart for Yong this morning.

Conflict Between Actors and Kiln Workers Turns into Tragedy

Dramas have been performed day and night in Ganyaozhen recently. The night before last, more than 20 kiln workers from the Pan Qiantai Tile Factory did not purchase tickets and tried to enter to watch the drama, but they were stopped by the gatekeepers. The kiln workers insisted on entering, and a conflict broke out between the two sides. The fighting was quite fierce. For a time, the audience fled, and the order was disrupted. The stage stools and utensils in the theater were destroyed. A portion of the kiln workers rushed to the actors' boat and dismantled the shed and sundries. At that time, the local small workers from the nearby kiln factory heard the news and came to help, gathering more than 100 people. The local security police were unable to suppress them. As a result, many people on both sides were seriously injured, especially Chen Xiaohua on the kiln worker's side, who was the most seriously injured and feared for his life. Zhou Apei on the actor's side also suffered serious head and chest injuries. He went to Suzhou for medical treatment that night. It is rumored that he died on the way. After the court examined Chen Xiaohua's injuries, he will file a lawsuit, but the actors are not willing to show weakness.

Local News

Major Hoke Flew a Condor Aircraft to Shanghai Yesterday

Only 35 Minutes Needed Between Shanghai and Hangzhou

And a Test Flight Will Be Conducted at Hongqiao Today

Came to Shanghai Again for Shanghai-Beiping Long-Distance Flight

According to Huadong News Agency, American aviator Major Hoke accompanied Pan Leiber of Union Aircraft Corporation to Hangzhou to inspect the aircraft. The aircraft has now been assembled. Yesterday at noon, Hoke flew it from Hangzhou to Hongqiao. Many instructors and mechanics from the Aviation Administration came with him. A test flight is scheduled to be conducted in Shanghai today, followed by a performance flight in Hangzhou the day after tomorrow. A long-distance flight between Shanghai and Beiping will be made in the near future. The following is a special report from the reporter of Huadong News Agency:

Installation Completed

The Curtiss Condor aircraft, after being transported to Hangzhou, was installed by Goss, the mechanic who came with Hoke, in just one week. Hoke himself went to Hangzhou on Thursday with Pan Hoke, the general manager of Union Aircraft Corporation, to inspect the aircraft in person. After checking the engine and fuselage, all parts were found to be in good condition. A test flight was conducted in the skies above Jianqiao yesterday morning.

Flew from Hangzhou to Shanghai

After the aircraft was assembled, in order to allow the people of Shanghai to understand the internal structure and equipment of the aircraft, it was flown from Hangzhou to Shanghai yesterday for a test flight, and then it will return to Hangzhou. Hoke flew the aircraft yesterday at 12:03 PM from Hangzhou Jianqiao Airport and arrived in Hongqiao at 12:38 PM, taking only 35 minutes. It circled the sky there once before landing. Those who came to Shanghai with Hoke on the aircraft included Pan Leiber, Goss, and seven or eight instructors from the Aviation Administration. After disembarking, Hoke and Pan Leiber took a car to Pan Leiber's residence to rest. The aircraft was parked at Hongqiao Airport.

Test Flight Today

According to the reporter of Huadong News Agency, after the aircraft flew to Hongqiao yesterday, Hoke is scheduled to conduct a test flight in Shanghai this morning or afternoon, flying around the city to wish the people of Shanghai good health. He will fly back to Hangzhou for a performance tomorrow (Monday). He will come to Shanghai again in a few days and depart for Beiping, making a long-distance round trip between Shanghai and Beiping on the same day, and then fly to Nanjing, Hankou, and other places.

The Reaction to Schurman's Speech: Maddi Expresses His Opinion

Yesterday's newspaper reported that Dr. Schurman, former U.S. Minister to China, gave a speech at the weekly luncheon of the American Club in Paris on the 5th, saying that China was still far from unification and that the central government's power only extended to five of the eighteen provinces, with the remaining thirteen provinces still in the hands of warlords unrestrained by the central government. Mr. Maddi, General Manager of the Maddi Motor Company, an American business in this port, was very displeased upon seeing this. Yesterday, he invited reporters from various Chinese and Western newspapers to publicly express his views as follows: "[Dr.] Schurman was well-informed during his tenure as Minister to China, which is beyond doubt. However, he has been away from China for a long time now and cannot truly observe the various progress that China is making, all of which is greatly related to China's unification. It should be known that China today is making progress in all aspects and should no longer be criticized with the perspective of years ago. I have been paying attention to China's efforts to unify. I feel that previously, the focus was entirely on political aspects, often neglecting geographical obstacles. However, due to the importance of transportation, work is now underway to connect the provinces. Therefore, I know that if Dr. Schurman were aware of China's recent developments, he would not make such a statement but would instead adopt an optimistic tone. Dr. Schurman should pay attention to the great progress in China's highway transportation and communication in recent years. He should understand the relationship of this force to the Chinese government's success in suppressing bandits and quelling rebellions in remote areas. He should realize the importance of modern transportation in suppressing the Fujian rebellion. Furthermore, he should pay attention to the Chinese government's plan and efforts to develop Xinjiang Province. If Dr. Schurman knew the progress China is making in geographically connecting the provinces, he would also recognize that China is moving toward a common goal socially, politically, and economically, and he would change his tone and realize he had misspoken. I believe that China's unification was previously misled by geographical obstacles. Fortunately, this weakness has been recognized. In recent years, thousands of miles of highways have been actively built, which has greatly helped the central government control the provinces. As for the highways that are being built and planned, it can be asserted that they will help the Nanjing government expand its power. Until recently, the United States was still a federation, but because of the development of road transportation and communication, it is now completely a single country. Given time, this road-building movement in China will surely achieve the same result. I think Dr. Schurman will also acknowledge this sooner or later. Over the years, I have been most interested in the development of transportation in China. I am especially pleased to see the central government building roads for the convenience of troop movements, thereby consolidating its position. But in the end, I feel that the progress made by the people of those areas in commerce and social interaction as a result of opening up new roads is even more commendable. Dr. Schurman should study this, and he will know that various forces in China are now working hard to achieve unification."

The Yuanshun Steamer Calls for Help

Lost at Sea off Ningbo Yesterday

Shanghai Company's Telegram Calls Go Unanswered

The Xinsheng News Agency reports that the Yuanshun steamer of the Datongxing Steamer Company, with a gross tonnage of 1,611 tons and a net tonnage of 1,016 tons, is dedicated to carrying cargo. It used to travel between Shanghai and Yingkou. This month, on the evening of the 4th, it loaded over 1,000 tons of cargo in Yantai and sailed to Xinghua, Fujian. The cargo mainly consisted of soybean oil, sorghum, and grain, and it also carried a small number of passengers traveling to Xinghua.

Accident Due to Fog

After the Yuanshun steamer departed from Yantai, it reached the waters off Ningbo at 12:45 AM yesterday. The route from Yantai to Ningbo is approximately 540 nautical miles. It encountered fog along the way and was sailing in the dark of night, losing its course and causing the accident. The shipowner instructed the wireless operator to send a telegram for help, but whether it was due to striking a reef or colliding with another ship is still unknown.

Sending a Telegram for Help

The Tokyo Radio Station received the Yuanshun steamer's call for help at 12:45 AM yesterday. At the same time, it also received the Jiahe steamer's call for help. The Japanese Salvage Company telegraphed the Mitsui Trading Company, the Shanghai salvage agent. The company then notified the Shanghai branch of Datongxing. The Shanghai company also received a telegram from the Yingkou headquarters yesterday morning, informing them that the Yingkou radio station had received the calls for help from the Yuanshun steamer and the Jiahe steamer or the Huafeng steamer.

Telegram Calls Go Unanswered

After receiving the telegram, the Shanghai branch of Datongxing immediately inquired with the Shanghai General Bureau of China Merchants Steam Navigation Company. At the same time, it requested the International Radio Station of the Ministry of Transportation to send telegrams to the waters off Ningbo, calling for the Yuanshun steamer. After four calls, the Yuanshun steamer's reply was still not received last night.

Jiahe is Fine

The Xinsheng News Agency reporter went to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's radio station yesterday to inquire. They learned that the station received a telegram from the Jiahe steamer from Fuzhou yesterday afternoon, stating that it was docked in Fuzhou. This proves that the Jiahe steamer did not encounter any danger. As for the Huafeng steamer, it does not travel to Shanghai, so it was impossible to verify. They also went to the Coastal Radio Station to inquire and learned that the Shanghai station also received the ship's call for help yesterday morning, but the audio was too low to understand.

Company Worries

The Shanghai branch of Datongxing is very anxious about the Yuanshun steamer case. After the telegram calls went unanswered, in addition to reporting to the Yingkou headquarters, it inquired with various parties in Shanghai, hoping to obtain accurate information about the Yuanshun steamer. According to those familiar with shipping affairs, the Yuanshun steamer's unanswered telegram calls indicate that it may have encountered an unforeseen event.

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Releases Statistics on the Monetary Business

Affected by the Economic Downturn, Business is Sluggish

Money Houses Mostly Adopt a Cautious Approach to Lending

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce released statistics on the monetary business, stating that since the opening of the five ports to foreign trade, Shanghai's commerce has become increasingly prosperous, and foreign trade has become increasingly developed. In order to maintain the market and assist the development of industry and commerce, the need for circulating finance must increase daily, and the turnover and exchange of silver and money must also prosper. Thus, the organization of money houses emerged as a financial regulatory mechanism. The agreement on interbank lending rates, the circulation of money house notes, and daily remittance transfers are all jointly decided by the monetary industry association. In the past, Nanshi's commerce was developed, and the business of money houses was also very developed. After the Taiping Rebellion, Nanshi suffered greatly, commerce declined, and the monetary business plummeted. Beishi, however, was located in the concessions and was not affected. To this day, the center of the monetary business has shifted from Nanshi to Beishi. The various money houses in Nanshi only follow the market trends of Beishi. The various money houses must borrow the services of the three major Chinese banks, the Central Bank, the Bank of Communications and the Bank of China for the collection and settlement of silver and money transactions with foreign banks, which is very inconvenient. Later, in order to safeguard the interests of the industry and facilitate the collection and settlement of silver and money, the monetary industry jointly remitted, and the Zhuang and Yuan character houses concentrated their finances and organized the Money Industry Joint Reserve in Ningbo Road, which was established on October 1, 1932. It is truly the central institution of Shanghai's finance. However, the conservative habits of the monetary industry are more serious than those of other industries. Although its organization is not as complete as that of banks and its capital is not as abundant as that of banks, due to its different nature, its credit lending and business scope far exceed those of banks. It has a long history, rich experience, simple procedures, and convenient contact. It can be accessed at any time from morning to night, which is quite suitable for the commercial habits of the Chinese people. Recently, in response to the trend of the times, it is planning to reform diligently and is also one of the three major financial pillars (foreign banks, domestic banks, and money houses). Therefore, it is still able to occupy a special and important position in the financial world and has the power to influence the finance of the interior. A total of 63 remitting houses and Yuan character houses in Nanshi and Beishi have been completely surveyed by the Chamber of Commerce. Based on their organizational situation and business overview, with the year 1932 as the standard, various statistics have been compiled and listed separately as follows:

The nature of fundraising and the amount of deposits and loans for the whole year are listed as follows: (Number of houses) Sole proprietorship, remitting houses 5, partnership, remitting houses 55, Yuan character houses 3, total 63, (Number of employees) remitting houses 1,823, Yuan character houses 103, total 1,926, (Capital) Sole proprietorship, remitting houses 1,780,000 yuan, partnership, remitting houses 15,457,496 yuan, Yuan character houses 450,000 yuan, total 17,687,496 yuan, (Amount of long-term deposits for the whole year) Sole proprietorship, remitting houses 4,700,000 yuan, partnership, remitting houses 32,068,246 yuan, Yuan character houses 2,700,000 yuan, total 39,468,246 yuan, (Amount of current deposits for the whole year) Sole proprietorship, remitting houses 8,550,000 yuan, partnership, remitting houses 12,073,981 yuan, Yuan character houses 2,700,000 yuan, total 122,323,981 yuan, (Amount of long-term loans for the whole year) Sole proprietorship, remitting houses 6,000,000 yuan, partnership, remitting houses 64,774,442 yuan, Yuan character houses 3,100,000 yuan, total 73,874,442 yuan, (Amount of current loans for the whole year) Sole proprietorship, remitting houses 6,200,000 yuan, partnership, remitting houses 75,889,704 yuan, Yuan character houses 2,100,000 yuan, total 84,189,704 yuan,

The business overview of Nanshi and Beishi is as follows: (Number of houses) Nanshi remitting houses 4, Beishi remitting houses 56, Yuan character houses 3, total 63, (Number of employees) Nanshi 107, Beishi 1,819, total 1,926, (Amount of various deposits for the whole year) Nanshi 8,344,000 yuan, Beishi 153,448,227 yuan, total 161,792,227 yuan, (Amount of various loans for the whole year) Nanshi 6,896,000 yuan, Beishi 151,168,146 yuan, total 158,064,146 yuan,

In total, there are 60 remitting houses and 3 Yuan character houses in the city. The remitting houses, due to their thicker capital and larger business, have joined the industry association (i.e., the Remitting General Association, also known as joining the gang), and thus have the name remitting houses. The Hen character houses, with their smaller scope and small loans and cash discounting, number 25. The Li character houses, which engage in interbank lending and buying and selling public bonds, number 12. The Zhen character houses, which engage in the collection and exchange of various types of gold and silver tickets, foreign money, number 34. It is estimated that there are 134 large and small money houses in the city. After the final settlement last year, 11 remitting houses, including Futai, added or changed their marks. 2 remitting houses, Tongtai and Dingtai, changed their signs. 2 remitting houses, Tongan and Hengxiang, and 2 Yuan character houses, Longtai and Dingda, closed down. Yifeng Zhuang has been expanded and changed to Zhengming Bank. Financial businesses should be operated in cooperation. Therefore, statistics show that partnerships are more common than sole proprietorships. Moreover, money houses bear unlimited liability, and their thick capital and strong resources allow them to adopt a more prudent business policy. However, in order to adapt to commercial customs and regulate finance, they place emphasis on credit. For example, a certain soy sauce shop owner does not have sufficient funds to use, nor can he use soy sauce as collateral to guarantee a loan from a bank. Money houses, however, can investigate whether his credit is reliable and arbitrarily grant loans to help him out of his predicament. This type of credit lending and overdraft is considered a dangerous business by the banking industry. In recent years, the international market has been sluggish, and the import and export industries have plummeted. Last year, the business was affected by the commercial downturn and suddenly felt sluggish. Most of them implemented austerity measures, and adopted a cautious approach to the loans of various businesses. The obstruction of social finance is due to the bankruptcy of the rural economy and the accumulation of inventory of various businesses. The need for sales stagnation, silver and money turnover is sharply reduced. Therefore, the results of the investigation are published in the newspaper for the reference of those who are concerned about the financial industry. (Xinsheng News Agency)

Two Industries Discuss Methods to Deal with Unscrupulous Merchants

The Glass Industry Association, due to the discovery that some unscrupulous individuals in the industry are selling inferior goods on the market, held a meeting yesterday and resolved to notify members and non-members to follow the instructions of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. The details are as follows: "To Whom It May Concern, the Japanese invaders have occupied the Northeast, massacring countless compatriots. Then they unleashed their troops on Shanghai, and the essence of the entire country was devastated. As a result, commerce is sluggish, and rural areas are bankrupt. We are all heartbroken and indignant, and we will never coexist with them under the same sky. We should permanently sever economic ties with them in order to save the fate of the country. However, recently, Japanese merchants have seen that Chinese merchants can be easily tempted by profits, so they have resumed their activities everywhere, and inferior goods have once again flooded the market. All of us in the industry should fulfill our national duty and resist to the end, without being moved. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce has already instructed the Woolen Goods Association on how to sanction the sale of provincial goods. This association has heard that there are also a few black sheep in the industry who openly sell inferior goods, so it has specially proposed the resolution of the fifth joint meeting of the executive and supervisory committees and sent a letter to members and non-members, urging them to be of one mind and not to sell inferior goods. It will also send personnel to secretly investigate. If there are any violators, this association will handle them in accordance with the instructions of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. A copy of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce's instructions on how to sanction the sale of inferior goods is enclosed for your reference and compliance."

The Vacuum Bottle Manufacturing Industry Association has recently learned that a large number of inferior vacuum bottles are planned to be dumped in this city. However, feeling that it is inconvenient to sell them openly, they are sacrificing themselves and using a group of unscrupulous merchants who are willing to be accomplices to promote the sales. Moreover, the fact that a few member factories have recently withdrawn from the association on the pretext makes us feel that there are suspicious clues. If we do not devise strict countermeasures, the domestic vacuum bottle industry will be greatly affected. Therefore, an emergency meeting was convened a few days ago. More than ten representatives from factories such as Lixing, Zhenye, Hanchang, Zhonghua, Tongchang, Xianghua, Sanxing, and Far East attended. As a result of the discussion, in addition to notifying all members to refrain from being accomplices and refusing to use inferior raw materials, a re-registration of members will also be conducted to begin a thorough investigation. If the above-mentioned facts are found to be true and there is solid evidence, the matter will be reported to the superior authorities for the most severe sanctions, and the names of the factories and managers will be published in the newspaper.

The receptionists are Mr. and Mrs. Chen Ce, Mr. and Mrs. Zhang Huichang, Ms. Shen Huifu, Mr. and Mrs. Jian Youwen, Mrs. Chen Qingyun, Liang Yunli, Chen Junpu, Deng Gongxuan, Liang Hancao, Mr. and Mrs. Xia Jinlin, Li Dachao, and Zhu Shaoping, etc.

The association believes that Mr. Wu not only contributed to the party and the country, but was also an international celebrity. Therefore, it has decided to have Lianhua Film Company send someone to film ten minutes of the memorial service today. It is also known that Guangzhou has also filmed a memorial service for Mr. Wu. Therefore, it is planned to compile the films and send them abroad for screening. Memorial Eulogy

The memorial eulogy reads, "Alas, the sea is vast, and the waves do not stop. The wind is bleak, and there is no calm branch. Sea and sky winds, holding much hatred. The spirit of gold and stone, alone cannot be ground down. When you first came into the world, [you were born at] the place of the ford of [the river of] Jin and the north. You were a talent of the south, truly born with insight. Endowed with ambition and grandeur, like Mount Tai and Mount Qiao. A bright and extraordinary child, with a singular spirit from an early age. Tracing your life, [we see] you abandoned a position of high honor. [You came from a] noble family with inherited virtues, with knowledge exceeding the grasp of five chariots. Like a bamboo shoot just sprouting, or an orchid just budding. You should be manifested in the world, to bring prosperity to your family. At a young age, you left the country, like a Kunpeng flying ten thousand miles. You began your career as a scholar, earning a reputation. You mastered foreign languages and studied poetry. You repeatedly emerged as an outstanding talent, bringing joy to your parents. Before you reached the age of twenty, you already had an outstanding reputation. You returned by raft, studying in the old capital. You painted mountains and water, purifying your mind and feelings. Your virtue increased with age, and your learning became great. You went to England and wielded a powerful pen. You protected the people, you were inspired to study law. You excelled in every examination, and your name matched reality. Your desire to help the people was as bright as the rising sun. When fortune turned in the Zhenyuan era, the Republic of China was founded. The uprising in Hubei was a righteous cause, and you responded with enthusiasm. You shouldered a heavy burden, and walked on thin ice. You shone with brilliance, dispelling the gloom. You planned in obscurity, and navigated the difficult steps of the nation. The new government was just beginning, and neighbors were doubtful. You declared heroic texts, as if breaking through the heavy fog. Your righteousness shook the Yellow Bell, and the four barbarians submitted. The foundation of the country was strengthened, whose merit was it? You were humble and unassuming, like a wild goose flying freely. When the plot to restore the monarchy arose, the wise were obscured and blocked. Your actions and choices showed integrity and a pure spirit. Heaven was not tired of chaos, and another restoration was brewing. You resigned and returned south, a steadfast stone. You protected the law in the southwest, opening up a new frontier. You were sent as an envoy to Paris, negotiating for peace. A famous father and son, repeatedly led the foreign office. You were diligent and vigilant, like the humble and auspicious six lines of the I Ching. You fought in debate, interspersing it with humor. You supported Zhang Jian's high reputation, with magnanimity and tolerance. You were loyal and benevolent, and you carried on the virtues of your ancestors. You assisted the capital, with the heart of a skilled craftsman. The [customs] case had been pending for a long time, and you broke it down with the right [tool]. You struggled with the law, weighing the pros and cons. You served within America, and attended The Hague. With reason and strength, your thoughts returned. Your words and speech were a model, a brilliant display of words. An easy going manner, accompanied by decisiveness. Deep and cultivated spirit. Essence acting as courage, independent tariffs. Treaties were meticulous, removing [foreign] concessions. The efforts were followed by [an effort to] to abandon the foreign taxes. What you have achieved is remarkable. To resolve internal strife, your public spirit was especially noble. You negotiated divisions, speaking and laughing at banquets. You did not dwell on your achievements. You made retirement easy. Far reaching aspirations, untroubled departure. Abandoning rank and riches, seeking poetry and the sea. Fragrant orchids and artemisia, the adornment of the gentleman. Then to the south, determined to open up Hainan. Looking forward to the Five-Five Year Plan, to develop this long-held aspiration. To develop this malarial island, and elevate it to the state of Yao. Who could have predicted such a fate? All of your great talents, and your noble friendship. Your past achievements and honors. You were cautious and tried to find ways to avoid issues, you disciplined yourself and did what was right, finally ending in a humble position, how could you die. The stars have suddenly fallen. coughs and not far [from death], You will ride cranes! [China's] Long Wall suddenly falls. You cannot be an example to the barbarians any more. The mountains and rivers stretch, who will succeed you? Alas. [Like] a whale in a cart of sea, for a long time the country lost a pillar [or a symbol of stability]. Like ants on [the walls of] the South Suburb, or mixing sparrows with tea. This man has ceased to be; the sleeping lion is hard to awaken. Literature has fallen, a waste of time to rest. alas. Flowers are easily faded, bubbles are difficult to make round. Where to cultivate character, when to hold arms? A moment in the universe, how can we prove fate? Clean sacrifices are given, looking to heaven and earth. alas."

Chinese and English Eulogies

The eulogy of the Central Executive Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang reads: "On the eighth day of April, in the twenty-third year of the Republic of China, the Central Executive Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang respectfully offers incense, flowers, and simple sacrifices to the spirit of Committee Member Wu Tiyun, saying: Alas, your talent and reputation made you a pillar of the nation. Your heroic demeanor and strong character were unique in your generation. You were able to overcome difficulties and had loyal integrity. How can we not mourn the loss of such a shining star? In the past, you, sir, had the experience and wisdom of an elder statesman. You protected the law and aided the times, providing advice and setting rules. You were a pillar of the nation, a model for all countries. You possessed those virtues. You maintained your reputation and had loyal integrity. You were the only voice at the Washington conference. You spoke with loyalty and fought against difficulties. You traversed a path full of thorns, and the surrounding nations praised you. You will be a hero for generations to come. While in Guangzhou, you diligently sought to govern and pacify the people. You cultivated loyalty and integrity, and you were steadfast. Your response to the moment was decisive, and the chaos was quickly suppressed. You traveled to foreign lands again, forgetting your own labor for the sake of the nation. You defended against insults, and your tongue was exhausted. Your mastery of public law was profound, and your righteousness was unique. You used the words of Zi Chan [a statesman from the Spring and Autumn Period] to solidify relations. Our nation is newly founded in every way. Grand plans and great laws all await to be adorned. We should all work together to pave a smooth road. Alas, when we heard this, our hearts were shattered. Alas, the vastness and turbulence of the Pearl River. The beauty of life has ended, but your legacy will endure. Your achievements will continue, and the sun and moon will shine on them. We offer this cup of wine, may you come and enjoy it."

National Government Eulogy

The National Government Chairman Lin Sen's eulogy reads: "On the eighth day of April, in the twenty-third year of the Republic of China, the Chairman of the National Government, Lin Sen, respectfully offers incense and music to the spirit of National Government Committee Member Wu Tiyun, saying: Alas, the land of Lingnan [Guangdong and Guangxi] endowed you with a loyal and outstanding spirit. You possessed great ambitions and talent, and you had inherited the fine virtues of your ancestors. Your broad learning combined Chinese and Western cultures. You supported the party and the nation, and you strengthened the foundation of our country. You negotiated and fought in debates. You fought for national rights, and the central government relied heavily on you. You attended the League of Nations, and you had a keen insight. You were eloquent and supported the weak. You repeatedly served as an envoy, promoting culture. The world competed to spread your message. Your writing made the prices increase, and the construction of Hainan began. You planned the mountains and forests, and you admired the Sichuan landscape. You were concerned about the people's livelihood, and you had grand plans. Before your great schemes could be implemented, how could Heaven have taken you away so quickly? Distant lands were moved, and all the seas were shocked. The pillars were broken, and the masses lost their model. Your merits will be engraved in bronze vessels, and your name will be recorded in the history books. National ceremonies will praise you, and your legacy will be passed down for thousands of years. The Pearl River is lush, and the Guangdong Sea is boundless. Your spirit seems to be connected to us, may you come and enjoy this."

The Funeral of Mrs. Cunningham Yesterday Morning

American Institutions All Fly Flags at Half-Mast to Show Mourning

The wife of U.S. Consul General in Shanghai, Cunningham, passed away in Hangzhou on the 4th due to a stroke. Her remains were transported back to Shanghai by car that evening. The funeral was held at the church on Jiujiang Road at 11:30 yesterday morning. Many Chinese and foreign officials and businessmen attended. The ceremony was simple. After the ceremony, the remains were cremated. Cunningham declined gifts of flowers from friends. Therefore, they were given cash to supplement the Cunningham Memorial Fund for the American Children's School in this port. By noon yesterday, a total of 5,386.20 yuan had been received. Yesterday, the U.S. Consulate General, the American Country Association, and other American institutions in this port all flew flags at half-mast to show mourning. The U.S. Consulate General effectively stopped working.

Sir Robert Hart, the Inspector General of Customs, had previously requested and been approved by the Ministry of Finance for a six-month leave to return to England to visit family. Seamen's Insurance Launched

Since its establishment, the Siming Insurance Company has successively launched various types of insurance, including fire, marine, and automobile, earning a notable reputation and enthusiastic support from policyholders. Recently, it has introduced a special "Seamen's Insurance" program specifically for workers serving on ships of all sizes, wharves, and related maritime industries. The method is annual, not extending to five or ten years. The insured amount is limited to between one hundred and one thousand yuan, with extremely low premiums that can be paid in installments, comprehensively considering the living conditions and capabilities of seamen. The simplicity of the procedures makes it easy for ordinary seamen to understand. Former section chief of the China Merchants Bureau, Hong Yanbin, has been specially appointed as manager, with the office located at No. 3 Xiang'an Lane, Gongguan Road. Insurance coverage began on April 1st, and it has been well-received by various shipping companies and seamen's organizations. Within a few months, the number of policyholders has reached over a thousand.

Master Mariners' Association Again Requests the Ministry of Communications to Refuse to Issue Certificates to Japanese Seafarers

Reportedly, Shipping Companies Hiring Japanese Seafarers

Indeed Issue Certificates

The Shanghai Master Mariners' Association previously reported that Minister of Communications Zhu Jiahe had verbally agreed to the request of the Japanese Consul in Nanjing to issue seafarer service certificates to Japanese seafarers who had not passed the Chinese examination and certification, totaling seventy to eighty people. This not only hinders the recovery of navigation rights but also contradicts the central government's past declarations promoting domestic shipping and rewarding Chinese shipping talents. They had petitioned Minister Zhu to promptly stop this and to sternly reject the Japanese request in order to protect navigation rights. Subsequently, they received a ministerial response stating that the claim that service certificates had been issued to Japanese seafarers who had not passed the examination and certification was purely a rumor and should not be taken seriously. The association considered this matter to be of great importance, not to be dismissed with empty words, directly affecting all seafarers and indirectly posing a significant threat to life and property. In recent years, accidents involving Japanese ships on Chinese waters have been frequently observed. The impact on the livelihoods of Chinese seafarers is not insignificant. Therefore, they launched an investigation and have now obtained some clues. Thus, they have submitted another petition to the Ministry of Communications, sent via express mail to Beijing, stating that the association has repeatedly investigated and learned from people close to shipping companies hiring Japanese seafarers that the Ministry has granted the Japanese request to issue certificates to Japanese seafarers who have not passed the examination and certification. The report from shipping companies hiring Japanese seafarers also confirms this, indicating that the Ministry's agreement to the Japanese request is not groundless. As this matter concerns the vital interests of shipping merchants and seafarers, it should be strictly rejected and the issuance of certificates should be stopped. This would be a great fortune for the shipping industry. They also requested instructions to be followed. This petition has just been submitted to the Ministry and has not yet received a reply in Shanghai.

The representatives of the Chinese delegation to the upcoming International Labour Conference, representing the government, labour, and employers, have been selected. Therefore, China will only submit a report to the conference to draw the attention of the representatives of various countries. It is not yet appropriate to announce other proposals in advance.

Long-Distance Telephone Service Between Shanghai and Danyang Opens Today

After a long period of preparation, all the engineering work for the long-distance telephone service between Danyang County, Jiangsu Province, and various districts of this city was completed yesterday. It is officially opened for calls today. The standard rate for calls from Nanshi, Zhabei, Zhenru, Wusong, Jiangwan, and Pudong in this city to Danyang is one dollar and twenty cents. The rate for calls from the Concession, Baoshan, and Nanxiang is one dollar and twenty-five cents. The time limit is still five minutes per call, and excess time will be charged according to regulations. Urgent calls will be charged three times the standard rate.

Directors Huang of Two Railways Admonish Employees

The Central News Agency reports that Huang Boqiao, Director of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration, issued a circular yesterday admonishing employees of all departments of the two railways, stating: "According to Dr. Sun Yat-sen's plan for material construction in his National Reconstruction Program, the development of transportation is of primary importance, with particular emphasis on railway construction. In January of this year, the Fourth Plenary Session declared that unification and construction are both absolutely necessary, and clarified that anything hindering unification and construction is hindering the great plan for national survival. In July of last year and February of this year, President Wang of the Executive Yuan and Chairman Chiang of the Military Affairs Commission jointly issued urgent telegrams emphasizing that there is nothing more urgent than production and construction. On February 19th, President Wang reported at the weekly memorial service of the Executive Yuan that railway construction was one of the key areas of recent construction work. Indeed, railway construction can both promote political unification and increase national production, making it the foundation of construction. The Directors of this Administration believe that for those engaged in railway construction, extending new lines is important, but improving existing lines cannot be ignored. The poor management of state-owned railways in our country has long been criticized by the people, leading to a lack of recognition of the importance of railways. If existing lines can be improved so that everyone can enjoy their convenience, then promoting new lines at the same time will be more welcomed by the people and easier to gain their support. Therefore, since taking office, the Directors of this Administration, following the instructions of the Ministry of Railways, have made improvement an urgent task. Last year, we first implemented the commercialization of state-owned railways and adopted a proactive approach to attracting business. Fortunately, thanks to the efforts of our colleagues, we have seen some success. Recently, we also revised the organizational structure of the traffic section to clarify the responsibilities of traffic personnel, which will further promote business. At the same time, we are reorganizing the Wusong Locomotive Factory to increase the efficiency of repairing and manufacturing locomotives and rolling stock to meet the needs of expanding business. As for the organizational structures of various departments, the engineering and accounting departments have also completed revisions and will be implemented soon. All of these are aimed at improving work efficiency. We have only slightly redistributed existing employees to ensure that personnel are properly assigned. Anyone who can abide by laws and regulations, work diligently, and achieve significant results will be strongly supported. On the other hand, we will also do our best to improve the welfare of our colleagues so that their physical and mental well-being and economic burden can be effectively addressed. All of us, my colleagues, must follow Dr. Sun Yat-sen's teachings, adhere to the Party and state's policies, and continue to work hard within the scope of our service to the railways to contribute to the nation's production and construction. The Directors of this Administration are willing to work together with our colleagues. If, unfortunately, anyone is ignorant of the nation's urgency and the importance of the railways, or takes actions that exceed the bounds of propriety and hinder the progress of the railways, they will be obstructing the nation's construction, betraying Dr. Sun Yat-sen's teachings, and violating the central government's policies. They will be considered undesirable elements in the railways and criminals against the Party and the state, and the Directors of this Administration will have no choice but to enforce the law. This is a circular to all departments and offices, which must be followed immediately, and all subordinates must be instructed to comply with it. This order is hereby issued."

Shanghai North Rice Carriers Strike to Protest the Cancellation of Wine Fees

The Municipal Party Department Orders the Rice Industry to Advise

Rice merchants in Shanghai North have announced the cancellation of the wine fee for rice carriers (i.e., the wine fee for carrying rice), leading to a strike. The details are as follows:

History of Wine Fee

In Shanghai, for every shi of rice, the rice carriers charge 24 cash. The same rate applies in both the northern and southern parts of the city. This practice has been in place for a long time. In 1912, the rice merchants paid the rice carriers 10 cash per shi of rice as a wine fee, the purpose of which was to help the rice carriers slightly in the process of carrying rice. In 1929, it was changed to 50 cash. In 1930, it was changed to 2 cents. When the price of rice rose to 25 yuan per shi, the difference between the weight and the amount charged became significant, so the rice merchants increased it to 2 jiao per shi. After the rice price crisis subsided, it remained at 2 cents. During the January 28th Incident, it changed to 5 cents. Since last year, it has been 3 cents.

Planned Abolition

Although rice carriers are nominally hired workers of the rice shops, the rice shops only provide meals and do not pay wages. Their income comes from the fixed 24 cash per shi, the wine fee, and commissions from the sale of rice (i.e., what is commonly called brokerage). Recently, due to the decline in rice prices, the rice merchants announced that they would cancel the wine fee from April 1st, which was opposed by the rice carriers. They went on strike on the 5th. Some rice merchants wanted to return to their hometowns, so they paid the fee to hire rice carriers. Some rice carriers waited for the fee to be paid before working. The bean and rice industry and the rice carriers' union have petitioned the Party and government agencies to request negotiations.

Rice Carriers Strike

Due to the dispute between the rice merchants and the rice carriers over the wine fee, some rice merchants announced that they would refuse to hire rice carriers, and the rice carriers went on strike. The Shanghai North Rice Sales Association, believing that this matter concerns the people's livelihood and fearing that a dispute over a small issue would affect social stability, has tried to mediate between the two parties, offering 2 cents per shi, but this was ineffective. Yesterday, rice carriers from Suzhou, Changshu, Jiangyin, Anhui, Yixing, and Jiangbei resumed work, but only a few from Wuxi did so. Yesterday, Fan Xisheng and Jin Guobiao, two rice merchants from Wuxi, had a dispute with the rice carriers at the wharf for preventing the transport of rice, but fortunately, no incident occurred.

Party and Government Handling

Fearing that the situation would escalate, the Municipal Party Department sent Secretary-General Jiang Huaisu, together with Fan Guoren from the Civil Affairs Section and Zhou Minggang from the Fourth Section of the Social Affairs Bureau, to investigate the truth yesterday afternoon. According to Jiang Huaisu of the Municipal Party Department, the Party Department believes that this matter is a dispute over a small issue, so it has ordered the rice industry to advise both parties in the hope of resolving it as soon as possible.

Rickshaw Contractors Jointly Petition the Municipal Council for Arrangement

Claiming to Bear Many Obligations and Not Just Profit Without Labour

Since the Public Concession's Municipal Council planned to reform the rickshaw industry in the special zone, deciding to revoke 2,000 licenses on July 1st and solicit new contractors, it has been repeatedly opposed by rickshaw owners and contractors. Zheng Guisheng, Zhu Deyao, Zhang Baofa, Huang Dengru, Shan Guideng, Qiao Wensheng, Xu Hongru, Yu Jiashun, Bian Qiren, Dai Yuean, and more than 1,500 other rickshaw contractors in the special zone jointly petitioned Municipal Council Director-General Chung Sze yesterday to withdraw the order to abolish rickshaw contractors in order to maintain their livelihoods. The original petition is excerpted as follows: "For the matter of jointly petitioning for the arrangement of positions to maintain the livelihoods of the people, we, Guisheng, etc., read in the newspaper yesterday that the Municipal Council's Board of Directors had adopted the proposal that the rickshaw rental should be 8 jiao per day and stipulated in the license regulations that this amount should not be exceeded, and that rickshaw pullers should also be licensed. We were shocked to hear this. We believe that the rickshaw owners bear a heavy responsibility in obtaining the rickshaw rental, such as providing dormitories, making equipment, lending money to attract rickshaw pullers, providing expenses to repay rent arrears, compensating for lost vehicles, and damaged parts. All kinds of obligations, all those in the rickshaw business know this, and it is not just profit without labour. The rickshaw pullers are also happy to take on the transfers, only requiring that there be a rickshaw to pull, not caring about the amount of the rickshaw rental. We previously heard that the Rickshaw Committee had proposed a rickshaw rental of 8 jiao. We have investigated and found that the market has its ups and downs, and prices also fluctuate. Therefore, the Council should only have supervisory power and not have the power to determine the amount. In the future, the new regulations should not include it. If there is no one responsible in this way, there will be no system. Guisheng, etc., have already jointly declared that the responsibilities are at stake. On March 14th, we submitted a petition requesting the Council to consider the livelihood issues of rickshaw contractors and to determine a rickshaw rental that is in line with the situation. We hope that you will understand. However, the original proposal is still being adopted without any increase. Rickshaw pullers must also be licensed to pull rickshaws, and there are restrictions. We do not know that rickshaw pullers may come and go to the countryside. In the future, we are afraid that there will be rickshaws without anyone to pull them. Then, the contractors will not be able to make a profit from this. They would not be willing to bear this heavy responsibility, which is tantamount to eliminating the position of rickshaw contractors and abruptly cutting off the livelihood of rickshaw contractors. It goes without saying that we must know that the rise and fall of all industries are not permanent. Looking at the reasons for the rise and fall, they are all caused by the pursuit of extreme circumstances. Only our rickshaw industry is currently in a period of prosperous operation. Although rickshaw pullers are said to be laborers, they support themselves and make a living. Compared with other laborers, they have a special situation. Therefore, there are tens of thousands of rickshaw pullers in this city, and there has never been a labor dispute. This is because the contractors are transferring between the rickshaw owners and the rickshaw pullers. We ask ourselves if we have made some contributions. Now, what crime have the rickshaw contractors committed that they should be eliminated? Observing the administrative authorities, they do not consider the large number of unemployed people in this city, and they will abruptly make rickshaw contractors, who have a safe livelihood, unemployed. They beautify it by calling it relief, which is not reasonable or reasonable. It is not seeking safety, but in fact, it is causing disputes. After thinking about it, we secretly believe that the Council has considered everything carefully and will never let the 1,500 or so rickshaw contractors suddenly cut off their livelihoods. We believe that there must be good arrangements to maintain the lives of the people. However, there is no clear expression, so we cannot help but be vigilant. Moreover, the most difficult thing to solve is that most of the contractors have a limited-year contract with the rickshaw owners. The current rickshaw rental cannot be terminated in the middle of the contract, which interferes with the law. How can the compensation within the term of the contract be obtained? In addition to continuously petitioning, which has not been approved, we should jointly continue to petition the Council to review and approve the process of how to arrange the positions of rickshaw contractors in detail in order to comfort the public's expectations, and also request the Council to indicate the legal basis for the dissolution of the contract, which we hope to be grateful for."

The association's notice to all members of the association states: 'Dear Sirs, In order to connect the feelings of members, the association has specially formulated travel and inspection group regulations, using collective efforts to investigate industries in various places, and to seek business development, to appreciate the scenery in various places, and to assist in physical and mental adjustment. Travel and Inspection Regulations

(1) The purpose of this group is to investigate industries in various places, inspect customs and cultures in various places, appreciate harmonious scenery, connect the feelings of members, to seek business development, and physical health. (2) All factory members of this association are eligible to be members of this group. (3) The number of members in this group is limited to 50 for each trip. (4) This group will travel once a month. (6) Each member participating in the trip must prepay all travel expenses, the amount of which will be determined temporarily (surplus will be refunded, deficiency will be made up for, other miscellaneous expenses will be self-prepared). (7) Those who wish to participate in the trip must notify the association three days in advance so that they can be registered. (8) Those who have registered and paid but are unable to participate due to unforeseen circumstances may ask someone to represent them. (11) When departing for the trip, several staff members from this association will be responsible for the reception. (12) If there are any imperfections in these regulations, they may be amended at any time."

Tenants of Baohua Lane Oppose Demolition of Houses

Police Prevent Landlord from Building a Fence

Guowen News Agency reports: The owner of Baohua Lane on Xinjihama Road in the Public Concession, Dehe Foreign Firm, issued a notice on December 31st of last year, ordering all tenants to vacate their houses before March 31st of this year in order to rebuild. The residents of the lane, believing that the houses are still intact, and in light of the current economic downturn and difficult market conditions, where all sectors are urgently seeking to reduce rents, how could they use the pretext of rebuilding to evict the residents? Until recently, the residents of the lane requested the First Special District Citizens' United Association to uphold justice. Unexpectedly, at 9:00 AM yesterday, the firm went back on its word and sent several workers on six trucks to nail bamboo fences in the lane. Upon hearing the news, all the women and children of the lane, more than 300 people, went out to block them. The situation became very tense for a while. Therefore, they immediately left and led all the tenants to Baohua Lane to hold an emergency meeting. A representative of the Municipal Council, Chen Jiufeng, attended. Yu Shilong was elected as chairman. After reporting on the process of petitioning the police station, it was resolved that the rebuilding period for the lane would be after three years. If the landlord puts pressure on them, they are willing to fight to the death. The meeting then adjourned.

Government Employees Who Commit Crimes Should Be Severely Punished with Increased Severity

Gao Maozhen's Theft Crime Was Only Punished with a Fine

The Prosecutor Has Filed an Appeal

Guo Maozhen, a supervisor of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, was accused of stealing several hundred yuan in cash and gold jewelry while searching the home of Li Ming, owner of the Gaochang Temple Jiangbian Road No. 678 small food shop, for gambling activities. Li Ming filed a complaint with the court, and the police chief of the Second District testified in court. Therefore, Gao was detained by the Prosecutor's Office. He was once released on bail by the Criminal Court, but because he avoided appearing in court, the guarantor was ordered to pay the bail money and hand Gao over to the court. The presiding judge, Liu Enrong, sentenced Li Ming to one year in prison and a fine of 200 yuan for operating a gambling den, while Gao's theft crime was punished with a fine of 660 yuan. After the verdict, Prosecutor Xie Lian argued that Gao was a government employee and should be severely punished with increased severity for committing a crime. The punishment of a fine would allow him to pay it off and go free. In terms of deterrence, there would be no substantial restriction on him, which would affect his repentance. To ensure equal treatment for officials and civilians, Prosecutor Xie detained Gao and filed an appeal, requesting the higher court to impose a suitable sentence according to the law to demonstrate fairness. Therefore, yesterday, the police were dispatched to escort Gao to the Suzhou Higher Court for trial. However, the original guarantor, Qiu Jinyun, was suddenly summoned to court again yesterday afternoon to inquire about the progress of the case during the litigation.

After the Pitou Workers' Strike, More Than 200,000 Pieces of Japanese Cloth are Shipped to Tianjin

Japanese Western Cloths Are Selling Well in North China

The First Batch is Shipped by the "Ichijin Maru"

The pitou (piece goods) lao sifu (foremen) of the Tianjin gang's customs brokerage firms in this city went on strike because the keke (customers) did not pay the cartage fee. The customs brokerage firms also stopped reporting and shipping pitou due to the rift caused by the strike. As a result, Chinese cloth could not be shipped to North China, and Japanese western cloth seized a good opportunity to be shipped in large quantities. The first batch, worth more than 200,000 yuan, has already been shipped. A reporter from this newspaper spoke with people in the industry yesterday and learned the following details of the incident and the current situation.

The Customs Brokerage Firms' Last Haul

Tianjin is a port where many pitou are shipped from Shanghai every year. Before 1920, the keke all had the customs brokerage firms handle it for them. For each piece of western cloth, after deducting the water freight and miscellaneous expenses, the customs brokerage firm could make a profit of two yuan and several jiao. In recent years, the keke have mostly purchased directly from textile factories or foreign firms, and the customs brokerage firms only handle the reporting and shipping of a portion of it. After the January 28th Incident, the market conditions deteriorated. The Japanese customs brokerage firms in Shanghai were the first to cut prices and abolish the lao sifu cartage fee of 2.8 jiao per piece, which was paid separately by the keke, and only charged the keke 2.95 yuan per piece for freight. The Chinese customs brokerage firms had to reduce their prices accordingly because of their location. Each piece of western cloth (generally called pitou) cost 2.52 yuan for water freight paid to the shipping company, 7 fen for baili, 2.4 jiao for dock cartage, and about 3 or 4 fen for other miscellaneous expenses. The customs brokerage firm nets less than 1 jiao per ocean. If there is any damage or shortage, they are responsible for compensation. Therefore, the customs brokerage firms' shipping of Tianjin pitou has reached a point where it is losing money.

The Difficulty in Resolving the Labor Dispute

Each customs brokerage firm has four or fewer lao sifu who load pitou. Historically, in addition to the freight, the keke paid the lao sifu another 2.8 jiao for each piece of Tianjin pitou they loaded. The customs brokerage firms did not ask about this. This year, since the Japanese first proposed the all-inclusive freight price of 2.95 yuan, the keke have also announced the cancellation of this 2.8 jiao subsidy. The lao sifu demanded it from the customs brokerage firms, but the customs brokerage firms earned less than 1 jiao. How could they agree? This led to the strike. This incident has been going on for many days. The Municipal Party Department and the Social Affairs Bureau have also mediated many times. The customs brokerage firms believe that this cartage fee must result in losses, and they cannot agree to it under any circumstances. They would rather appropriately increase the wages of the pitou lao sifu, but they cannot pay the cartage fee. The workers insist on getting the cartage fee, and they do not care about the wage increase. Therefore, the strike is difficult to resolve.

The Customs Brokerage Firms Have Also Stopped Shipping

Yufengsheng, which has always shipped the most Tianjin western cloth, has decided to give up the business of reporting and shipping pitou and switch to reporting and shipping miscellaneous goods since the strike occurred. Fuji Customs Brokerage Firm, which has heard various unfavorable rumors after the strike, has temporarily suspended its business. It does not report or ship Tianjin pitou in general, and it has also temporarily stopped reporting other miscellaneous goods. It would rather temporarily lay off its employees than continue to make a meager profit. Recently, since the new customs regulations were announced, all keke can freely report and ship goods after paying a deposit, which has greatly impacted the business of the customs brokerage industry. Once an accident occurs, they all adopt a passive attitude.

Japanese Cloth Suddenly Improves

According to people in the customs brokerage industry, at least 100,000 pieces of pitou western cloth worth 20 million yuan are shipped from Shanghai to Tianjin every year. In recent years, after the boycott of inferior goods, domestic cloth has occupied a considerable share of the market in North China. The current strike has made it impossible to report and ship domestic cloth. The Tianjin gang, due to market demand, cannot immediately stop doing business, and Japanese cloth has seized this good opportunity to be shipped to Tianjin. The Japanese textile factories in this city are using Japanese ships, and Japanese customs brokerage firms are reporting and shipping on their behalf. Large quantities have already been shipped. The first batch of Japanese cloth after the strike was the 1,600 pieces of the "Ichijin Maru" to Tianjin, which were reported and shipped by Hirata Japanese Customs Brokerage Firm, worth more than 200,000 yuan. There are also large quantities of Japanese cloth to be shipped to Tianjin on the "Changsha Maru" and other Japanese ships.

Domestic Cloth is Obstructed

According to people in the industry, this strike not only creates opportunities for Japanese goods, but also greatly impacts the sales of domestic cloth from various factories in North China. The workers used by the Japanese customs brokerage firms to report and ship Japanese pitou are also Chinese workers who specialize in loading Japanese goods. If these workers also join the strike, the Japanese are preparing to hire Japanese or Russian workers to replace them, so as not to interrupt transportation. China will be subject to the double pressure of strikes and suspension of transportation.

Zhang Shiliang, Who Trafficked Red Pills, Is Convicted

Sentenced to Two and a Half Years and Fined 1,000 Yuan

Zhang Shiliang, a local, specializes in trafficking red pill drugs and secretly set up a red pill manufacturing facility on the upper floor of the Shenfeng Fruit Store at 473 Henan Road. Recently, Lu Liankui, the Chinese superintendent of the Narcotics Division of the General Inspectorate, learned of this and dispatched Chinese detectives Liu Shaokui, Song Bingzheng, Tanmu Zhang Yunhong, and Bao Detective Xu Guirong to wait at the intersection of Henan Road and Tianjin Road at 12:30 PM on the 27th of last month. He was apprehended and more than 30 bags of red pills weighing a total of 186 liang were seized. He was immediately taken back to the police station. Under interrogation, he confessed to the location of the manufacturing facility. A search was conducted at the address, and another five to six thousand liang of red pills and pill blocks, as well as raw materials and machinery, were found. On the morning of the 28th, he was sent to the Criminal Court of the First Special District for trial. However, because the principal offender was at large and still being pursued, the police lawyer requested that the trial be postponed. Yesterday was the date for the continuation of the trial. Presiding Judge Liu Yugui presided over the trial in Criminal Court One. First, the police lawyer presented the case, questioning the defendant. According to the confession, he only worked as a tea servant in the drug facility for eight or nine days and did not know much about the details. As for the principal offenders, he knew that Tang Gengsheng, Fang Shaohua, Wang Agen, and Yao were partners. All matters related to the red pill ingredients were handled by Miao Hongchang. On the 27th, Miao only instructed him to send the red pills to the entrance of Caitongde on Tianjin Road. He did not know who to hand them over to. Miao himself was also present at the time. After the police lawyer presented his opinion, Judge Liu immediately declared the end of the debate and sentenced Zhang Shiliang to two years and six months in prison and a fine of 1,000 yuan.
