European Marriage Introductions

— Chi

Indeed, marriage is not the central problem for women, but from an environmental and physiological point of view, marriage is one of the important problems for women. Due to environmental and traditional reasons, women usually have timid personalities and shy habits. Although there are many opportunities for women to socialize in society, due to timidity and shyness, it is often difficult to obtain satisfactory free love with men. Moreover, occasional encounters are not satisfactory opportunities. Therefore, in various European countries, there are organizations that introduce marriages, established in large cities. These organizations enable women to have a more accurate grasp of solving marriage problems and easily achieve the ideal of free love between men and women.

In China's feudal era, marriages were controlled by parents' orders and matchmakers' words. Even today, although the trend of free love has greatly increased due to the changes of the times, the matchmaker system still remains in society. In addition, due to incomplete freedom and improper love, many tragedies have occurred, and women suffer more from its drawbacks. Therefore, the organization of marriage introduction agencies is also worth considering as one of the issues that should be addressed in our country's women's problems. Now, I will list examples from several countries below:

In England, there are nationally established marriage introduction magazine companies. The books published by these magazine companies are all magazines that discuss marriage problems, and experts write them. If there are any difficulties in your marriage problems, you can inquire about solutions. If marriage problems cannot be solved or there are no standards for choosing a spouse, you can also inform the editors of your background, occupation, age, appearance, temperament, etc., and experts will provide guidance in the magazine. The magazine company has two types of mailboxes: A for men and B for women. If you want to find a partner of the opposite sex, you can publish all your information in the magazine, stating the number of the designated mailbox. When a member of the opposite sex believes that you are a suitable match, they can send you a letter.

In Germany, there is a famous marriage newspaper that also completely discusses marriage problems. If you are looking for a spouse, you can publish your background, environment, and the background and environment you are looking for in the newspaper, and inform the newspaper of your name and address. If someone responds, they can send a letter to the newspaper, stating the number of the advertisement. The newspaper will keep the names and addresses of the correspondents confidential.

France also has a marriage newspaper, with similar methods to Germany. However, the marriage newspaper company has the right to check the truthfulness of the senders to avoid malpractice. Although the fees are high, fraud and other incidents are considerably reduced. As for Italy, there are also similar organizations, but due to poor management, problems have arisen, so these organizations have not been very developed in recent years.

Child Rearing and Wet Nurses

— Liang

Due to the low standard of living and lack of hygiene knowledge, the Chinese people have never been very concerned about child-rearing issues. Regarding this point, we only need to check the infant mortality rates in various regions to believe it.

Although there are no accurate statistics on infant mortality rates in our country, if we compare them with those in Europe and America, the rate is shockingly high, which is recognized by most people.

There are many reasons for the high infant mortality rate. What I want to talk about here is the issue of hiring wet nurses, because hiring wet nurses is one of the most important reasons. In the past, the practice of hiring wet nurses can be said to have been nonexistent. Even if it existed, it was only when the infant's biological mother did not have enough breast milk, and a neighbor or relative with sufficient milk temporarily came to breastfeed. This had the nature of mutual help and did not have the formal meaning of employment. The phenomenon of hiring wet nurses can be said to have only occurred in capitalist societies. The reason is that, on the one hand, the wives and grandmothers of the propertied class, in order to pursue personal leisure and maintain their "beauty," have to entrust the care of their infants to others; thus, the demand for wet nurses arises. On the other hand, due to the bankruptcy of the countryside, impoverished women who cannot make a living in the countryside, although they also have their own biological infants, are forced to come out to work as wet nurses due to the pressure of life; this is the supply of wet nurses, which comes from this. With demand and supply, it is no wonder that hiring wet nurses has become a trend in modern society, especially in cities.

Originally, hiring a wet nurse is not objectionable if it is due to insufficient breast milk from the mother or occupational constraints; however, if it is because of being busy with social engagements and being accustomed to idleness, as well as the superstition that not breastfeeding one's own child is a kind of "preserving appearance," then it is absolutely not right. We mothers should understand that hiring a wet nurse is a last resort; do not hire a wet nurse unless it is absolutely necessary. Because, according to general statistics, the sacrifices of infants on the issue of hiring wet nurses are truly alarming. The harm of hiring wet nurses to infants can be said in four ways:

(1) The incompatibility of milk quality. The breast milk of the biological mother has a natural relationship with the infant's body and is very suitable. However, the wet nurse's milk is not. Due to the different times of delivery or the different concentrations of milk, there are often unexpected concerns when the infant drinks it.

(2) Lack of child-rearing knowledge and emotion. Wet nurses mostly come from poor rural households. Because their lives are simple, they do not know how to pay attention to hygiene and lack child-rearing knowledge. Therefore, they do not know how to guide reasonably in the infant's eating, clothing, playing, and other matters, which has a non-trivial impact on the infant's body and habits.

(3) The danger of infectious diseases. If, unfortunately, a wet nurse is hired and happens to have infectious diseases such as scabies, trachoma, tuberculosis, or syphilis, then it goes without saying that the infant will be infected.

In this way, it is best not to hire a wet nurse unless it is absolutely necessary.

However, in reality, as long as the current social system is not fundamentally changed, this phenomenon of wet nurse employment cannot be eliminated. Currently, as a stopgap measure, to avoid infants from getting sick and dying, we can only think about the following when choosing a wet nurse:

(1) The first condition for a wet nurse is that she must be healthy, especially that she must not have any suspicion of infectious diseases such as trachoma, tuberculosis, or syphilis. Regarding this point, it is best to ask a doctor to check it.

(2) The wet nurse's delivery date should not be too far from the date of birth of one's own infant; it is best to be within two months.

(3) The wet nurse must be kind-hearted and her temperament must be gentle. Those who are impatient and irresponsible should not be used.

(4) The wet nurse must usually pay attention to cleanliness and must have some hygienic knowledge of child rearing (as long as she is responsible, this point can be instructed in detail by the infant's biological mother on a daily basis).

American Cotton Rebounds Due to Delivery

Yesterday's American cotton market initially fell due to foreign merchants selling, and then rebounded due to spot merchants buying and shorts covering. As a result, spot prices rose by 10 points, and futures rose by 1 to 11 points. Liverpool cotton spot prices fell by 4 points, and futures fell by 2 points. Egyptian cotton spot prices remained unchanged. The Bombay cotton market fell due to long positions closing. As a result, Pingar, Omra, and both fell by 2 rupees and 2.5 cents, and Bai Luo Creek fell by 2.5 rupees. Original telegram recorded on the left (6th telegram):

American Cotton Awaits the Final Development of the Peng Case

New York telegram on the 6th, reporting on the cotton market in the past week, said that the cotton market was calm last week, all waiting for the final development of the Peng Hai case and other stimuli. Within this week, it had rebounded 40 points from the lowest price, and then a small number of southern sales and long positions closing occurred, and the price fluctuated again. There were also some arbitrage sales to resist foreign cotton, but the pressure was not great. Spot demand remained sluggish, but the base price was stable. Japanese purchases were recent, and those related to the Far East had news of buying new cotton. The first week's weather report of the season showed that the progress in Texas and South Georgia was good, but some areas in the central and northern cotton belts had not yet been completed. Although raw cotton was uncertain, the cotton cloth market was better.

Food

Beiyang Flour is Selling Well

New Stockpilers of Flour are Emerging

Yesterday's flour market was in good shape. Due to the strong sales of Beiyang flour in recent days, the residual flour stored in the market has been completely shipped out, totaling as many as 200,000 bags. The appetite has been good recently, and attention has been paid to recent standards. With the revitalization of customers, the factories have once again adhered to not selling, and people's hearts are unanimously optimistic. It has also attracted new stockpiling and short covering transactions. This month, the spot flour is active and even more firm. The closing price rose by 1.75 cents, September rose by 1.25 cents, May and July rose by 0.75 cents each, and June and August rose by 0.5 cents each.

Foreign Goods Arrive at the Port

Futures Fall by Three Cents

Yesterday's wheat market had a slight increase in foreign wheat. 期wheat had merchants throwing in套, and the market also tended to weaken. People's hearts were also empty. Because there were foreign wheat orders arriving in Shanghai, and there were still discussions about continuing to borrow American wheat. After the opening, all months saw a downstream trend. The closing price was down 3 cents in April, down 3 cents in June, and down 1 cent each in July and August. Spot wheat inventories have arrived adequately, and factory conversions are also active. Yesterday, Fuxin, Shenda, and others bought 6,300 bags. Shandong and other high wheat were 3 yuan and 57 cents, Yingzhou, Gaoyou, and other second-class wheat were 3 yuan and a half, and the middle and second-class wheat were reduced accordingly. The market remained stable.

Late Rice is Highly Determined and Medium Rice is Reduced

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, the sources from various gangs surged, totaling more than 80 numbers (more than 8,000 stones). Among them, late rice was the most abundant, and thick japonica rice and various colors accounted for half. The sales of late rice have also become smoother. At the beginning of the market, Nanyang, Xiamen, Fuzhou, and other gangs took action to purchase, and the Beiyang gang was particularly strong until the closing. A total of 2,450 bags of Qingjiao, Songsi, Xilian, and other goods were delivered. However, customers saw the surge of goods and were very strict in their selection. High-quality goods were slightly taken, and there was an ambiguous attitude towards medium and second-class goods. The eating plate problem was therefore difficult to relax. Fortunately, the sellers insisted, and a situation of high determination and medium depreciation appeared. For example, the price of Qingjiao and Songsi was stable, and the price of Fengjing and Xilian was slightly modified by 2 or 3 cents. The japonica rice from Changbang, Sutong, and Nangang was transformed into a strong urban and rural store appetite, resulting in a balance between arrival and sales. However, because there were still remaining goods, the general trend was slightly soft, and the market price was neither honored nor disgraced, and remained at the old level. The status of Duyangjian was determined, and the sales of Bianyin Yuan suddenly became prosperous, and the market atmosphere turned up slightly.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, 18 or 19 ships arrived from various places in Hexia. Due to the problem of斛师 in the market sales, it has not been completely resolved, so there are very few peers opening斛. There are few buyers and sellers on the market, and few transactions are made. Foreign Zhuang Rapeseed is Traded in Batches

Soybeans Still Lack Stability

Rapeseed transactions are mostly carried out in secret, so there is a lack of real information, and the market situation is flat and tired. At present, there are still 450,000 bags of Pinghu goods at the bottom, and most of the properties are fixed, and the market price is not easy to over-repair. Yesterday, I heard that 1,000 bags of Pinghu goods were traded, and the price was 4 liang and 2 and a half qian. According to the old rules, there are still 2 qian in the market, but it is not certain. The trend of soybeans is still difficult to stand, although the source is small, but the sales are light, yesterday the total market traded 6 cars, so people's hearts can not help but weaken, the market fell by 2 or 3 cents again.

Piece Goods

Tianjin Qing Gang Purchases Raincoat Cloth

The retail and wholesale transactions of wool and velvet were still booming yesterday. The market price of raincoat cloth was slightly firm, especially single-sided open water beauty, because the Qingdao and Tianjin gangs searched for it. Yuanzang colors are especially lively. Yesterday, the industry sold 14 boxes of thick and thin raincoat cloth, including 9 boxes purchased by the Tianjin gang and 5 boxes by the Qingdao gang. The inner single-sided open water beauty accounted for 11 boxes, elephant skin 元常 blue-grey thin goods only had 3 boxes. Ningfeng spot goods and Yikang Changji both had sales. There were 7 boxes of brokers' resales. Silk Tea

China Silk Seeks External Development

Silk factories in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces have recently experienced slow sales of Chinese silk, which is purely due to the lack of a perfect organization in the sales aspect, so when foreign cities need it, there is nowhere to buy Chinese silk. It is believed that without organizing a large-scale raw silk foreign trade agency, it is impossible to save the current crisis. Therefore, it is specially recommended that the Ministry of Industry and Commerce set up a sales general office in Shanghai, and set up sales offices in Lyon and New York to observe the silk sales situation in France and the United States at any time and the market price situation, and to identify factory silk to various silk factories in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, and transport it for direct sales.

Shen Bao Amateur Weekly

The Process of Chinese Directors in the Shanghai Municipal Council

— Gongpu

Last time, this reporter wrote an article discussing the Shanghai municipal election issue. The main point of that article was to explain that citizens should pay close attention to municipal elections and should not take them lightly, in order to promote citizens' interest in participating in politics. Now, I will briefly describe the origin of the Shanghai Public Concession Municipal Organization (i.e., the Municipal Council, its English name being shangbaemunicepalcouncil, which is [Shanghai Municipal Government]) and the process of Chinese people joining the Municipal Council as directors, so that the general public can understand why there are Chinese directors in the Municipal Council and what efforts we should make regarding Shanghai's municipal affairs.

The opening of Shanghai as a concession was based on the Treaty of Nanjing in 1843, and the Treaty of Nanjing was a treaty signed between our country and Britain after the Opium War. Everyone knows this, so there is no need to elaborate. However, the Shanghai Municipal Council did not exist immediately after the establishment of the concession. It went through many transformations to form its current organization. The original purpose of the 1845 Land Regulations was only to explain the relationship between Chinese and British people's land property, without any provisions for municipal organizations. Therefore, at that time, municipal affairs in the concession and the management of expatriates from various countries were still the responsibility of the consuls of each country. The regulations only stipulated that "[the British Consul may appoint impartial merchants to organize a [Road and Wharf Committee]]." Later, during the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom Rebellion, the number of Chinese people fleeing to the concession increased, and expatriates from various countries were afraid of being disturbed by the war. Foreigners all felt the danger of not having a unified organization. As a result, the 1854 Amended Land Regulations were created, which contained provisions for municipal organizations. This was the initial organization of the current Municipal Council. However, the power of this organization at that time was only to have the power to tax and police. It was not a true municipal government. The completion of a true municipal government was the result of gradual evolution later. This article is intended to explain the issue of Chinese representation, so it only describes the origin of the Municipal Council. As for its evolutionary process, it is not necessary to discuss it, so it will not be discussed.

In the Land Regulations passed by foreign taxpayers in 1866, there was a principle of Chinese representation, but it has not been implemented. The reason why it was not implemented, according to the Feitang Report, is that no one knows until now. However, although he did not explain the reason, two sentences are worth noting. He said: "[On the other hand, the proposal made in 1866 may have been too early considering the actual situation at the time. At that time, it may not have been easy to find one or two leading Chinese people in the concession who were willing to take responsibility for serving on the advisory committee... Before 1906, the Chinese people in the Public Concession had never clearly demanded it]." According to this, the fact that the municipal administration was completely monopolized by foreigners was actually due to the fact that our own people were not good, neglecting their rights and not intervening. Later, foreigners, seeing the ease with which the Chinese could be dealt with, did not pay attention to our demands, and the reason for this was also this.

Now, the process of our people's request to join as representatives will be described as follows:

(1) In 1906, the Chinese people made a request to the Municipal Council based on the aforementioned regulations, hoping that the Municipal Council would accommodate the opinions of the Chinese side and hire Chinese people as consultants. The origin of this request was due to the so-called "Mixed Court Riot" at that time. Why did this riot happen? According to Feitang, it was caused by the dispute between the Municipal Council and the Chinese authorities, but why would the dispute between Chinese and foreign authorities cause "rioters" to riot? Although Feitang did not mention this at all, we can imagine that there must have been another reason. However, this request was unanimously approved by the directors of various industry associations, and the proposed Chinese Merchants Advisory Committee was "[purely representing the Chinese business community]" and "[representing the banking and commercial interests of the Chinese people in the Public Concession]," not for the general public to enjoy municipal benefits. However, even this request was rejected by the foreign taxpayers' meeting, and the result was not implemented.

(2) The second formal proposal was submitted in 1915, which was one of the conditions contained in the draft treaty for the expansion of the Public Concession discussed by the consular countries and the Chinese authorities at that time. The main point was "[using the employment of consultants as a satisfactory solution]," not increasing the number of Chinese directors. The Municipal Council solemnly stated: "[The reason for its recognition is to resolve the difficulties it has repeatedly encountered, not for the Chinese to interfere in the administration of the concession]." However, although this request was accepted by the foreign taxpayers' meeting, it was still not implemented in fact.

(3) In 1920, due to the increase in municipal taxes, there was a riot, so the Joint Association of All Roads Business Circles requested the Municipal Council to add Chinese representatives. At that time, although the Municipal Council approved the consultant system, it strongly opposed the addition of Chinese directors, because their opinion was: "[In fact, the Chinese people's residence here can almost be said to be due to tolerance, and there is no legal right to demand participation in our administration]." After the matter was brought to the attention of the leading consul by the Chief Executive, and approved by the foreign taxpayers' meeting, it was formally established, but this association had no achievements or results whatsoever.

(4) In 1925, due to the May 30th Massacre, the anti-imperialist trend was high, and foreigners, threatened by this, agreed to the request to increase the number of Chinese directors to three. However, due to the dispute over the number of seats, it was delayed for two years before the Chinese directors officially took office.

(5) In 1930, the number of Chinese directors increased to five. At this time, there were a total of fourteen directors, with nine foreigners.

In summary, there are three points that we should deeply recognize and be aware of, namely (1) The Westerners' permission for Chinese people to join the Municipal Council is entirely based on their convenience in handling affairs, and not based on the principles of democracy, or recognizing the rights of the Chinese people. They do so because the majority of the concession residents are Chinese, and Chinese taxes account for more than 55% of the Municipal Council's tax revenue;

(2) The reason why Westerners do not accommodate the demands of the Chinese people is because the Chinese people themselves give up their rights, and the requesters are only a few people;

(3) Only when the people are united and make firm demands can Westerners be persuaded to comply. Gentlemen who advocate national revival and democratic politics must not neglect this point in order to be successful.

Life

［A Long-Term Worker's Wage, a Pipe of Tobacco!］

— Wang Xizhe

In my hometown, Yixing, the situation is roughly the same as in other counties in the south of the Yangtze River. Long-term workers are divided into four types: those who herd cattle are called "young lads," those whose energy development is half-mature are called "stable lads," the young and strong are formal long-term workers, and the old, weak, and sick are in the ranks of the disabled. Among them, long-term workers are the main force in farming.

The annual salary of a long-term worker ranges from twenty-one or two yuan to twenty-seven or eight yuan. Only families where the boss cannot personally work in the fields hire a "foreman lad" for thirty yuan a year to replace the boss in fulfilling the supervisory duties. This is mostly done by the boss's relatives, nephews, or cousins.

The annual work of a long-term worker is to go to the fields before dawn during the busy farming season, and return home groping for farm tools at night. If they are sick for three days, they have to find a substitute, paid for by the long-term worker. When field work has not yet started or has been completed, they have to transport manure to the town, go up the mountains to cut firewood, go down to the river to get mud, row boats, push carts, weave straw goods in the cow shed, weave bamboo objects, and beat and . There are very limited days off. As for the hardships of long-term workers, such as the wind and rain in spring and the plum rain season, the sun and heat in summer and autumn, and the wind and snow in winter, my pen cannot describe them.

The combination and treatment of long-term workers and bosses are as follows: around the Winter Solstice, in the early morning teahouses in the village or town, a third party acts as an intermediary to introduce the two parties to discuss work. After the wage is agreed upon, the long-term worker has to invite the boss and the intermediary to dinner. On the fifth day of the first lunar month of the following year, the boss sets up a rich feast to invite all the long-term workers and the intermediary. This is called "tying the nose wine," meaning that like a耕牛, the nose is tied with a rope, and they have to bury themselves in work. If they look up or wag their tails, the boss's whip can be used at any time, until the evening of the twenty-fourth day of the twelfth lunar month when they have prepared all the New Year's food for the boss, they leave the boss's house like wild dogs with their tails between their legs after eating some rice flour dumplings. Throughout the year, they eat three meals a day: white porridge in the morning, rice at noon, and vegetables in the evening, as well as taro or yam porridge, coarse rice dumplings, and noodle soup. During the busy farming season, there are oil pancakes and liquor brought to the fields at noon, those with a big temper often get to eat them.

The way long-term workers withdraw their wages and take holidays is as follows: after agreeing on the wage and inviting the boss and intermediary to dinner, they can withdraw one-quarter of the wage in advance. Later, on holidays such as the fifteenth day of the first lunar month, the eighth day of the second lunar month, the day after transplanting rice seedlings, the twenty-third day of the sixth lunar month, the fifteenth day of the seventh lunar month, and the thirteenth day of the ninth lunar month, they can withdraw half a yuan each time to go to the streets for a day of fun and drink old wine. When they return, they have to buy some food for the young boss as thanks to the boss's wife for mending their torn clothes a few times. The rest of the money is all spent on a yellow tobacco pipe. Today, the boss goes to the street to buy one hundred copper coins' worth of yellow tobacco and a pack of matches, and the next day it is another one hundred and thirty copper coins. The boss records it in the books, and by the time the autumn wind rises, they have already owed the boss a tobacco debt beyond their wages. Therefore, they have to work extra diligently, hoping to get the money to pay for the tobacco in advance before discussing the work, in order to mortgage tomorrow's wages. In this way, those who have been long-term workers all their lives have no way to find a wife to pass on their lineage. Those who have wives bring their little sons to the east family to herd cattle, while their wives live in Shanghai to work in factories or go to matchmaking agencies. Those who do not have wives, after reaching middle age, seeing themselves coughing and hunching over, vow to throw away their tobacco pipes and quit smoking yellow tobacco, and have affairs with widows to have a son or half a daughter to replace themselves as long-term workers. Those who cannot quit their smoking addiction grow old, get sick, and quietly die in a dilapidated temple by the village. This is the life of a long-term worker who has been praised by peers and bosses for planting ten thousand seedlings in a straight row and stepping on the high and urgent waterwheel of nine people per shaft, and has been said to have earned high wages and smoked big pipes of tobacco!

[Money earned through evil deeds will be burned by heavenly fire; money earned through commerce lasts thirty years; money earned through farming lasts forever.] This is a true expression of the farmers' feudal consciousness of accepting their fate. However, the wage of a long-term worker is only worth a pipe of tobacco!

[Rice flour dumplings on the twenty-third, rice on the twenty-fourth (using rice flour dumplings on the twenty-third of the twelfth lunar month to send off the Kitchen God, and rice on the twenty-fourth), the long-term worker eats and quickly rolls away! A broken umbrella in the corner of the door, two leaky nailed shoes under the door sill, the long-term worker grabs them and rolls away. The big boss calls the little boss, give him three flat loads, the long-term worker is beaten and stumbles, crying all the way! Throwing away the umbrella, dropping the nailed shoes, the boss's wife takes them to exchange for candy to deceive the children.] This children's song that the young bosses often sing every year-end, I used to sing to the long-term workers thousands of times when I was a child, and today I feel its bitter taste.

Yin Mountain

— Bao Hei

In the warehouse.

Large wooden boxes, barrels, steel bars, cocoon bags - a big pile, a big pile, high.

There is no window, the wind drills in from the cracks in the lead skin roof, calling "whoosh whoosh..."

Even on a sunny day, with the sun outside, work is still done under the glow of fifteen osram lights. A place that has lost nature! It is always bleak.

Four or five stories, a tall western-style building, but without teak paneling, patterned glass windows, or waxed floors, no beautiful decorations at all. Here, there is only cement floor, white powder sand walls, and rough pillars that chafe the skin. Here, there are always piles of goods stacked, on this side, on that side, the outlines of the goods piles rise in the space, pitch black.

Here, it is always gloomy and eerie.

"Yin Mountain!" everyone calls it.

Everyone lives in Yin Mountain, breathing in the foul air, smelling the fishy stench. The air is always suffocating, as I said, there are no windows here.

When it is uncomfortably humid, they want to stroll out to the corridor, want to light a cigarette, but immediately, the red ground white character enamel sign "No Smoking" comes into view, and every character seems to stare with a majestic eyeball.

Majestic eyeballs can sometimes be found on the faces of some noble merchants.

Every time, every time, the coolies walk to the door, they snuff out the cigarette butts and secretly stuff them into their belts.

Come! "Oh yo! Oh yo! Oh yo!"

When they load a thousand pounds of cargo onto their shoulders, this cry full of vitality bursts out from their rough throats.

In the warehouse, the roar will not stop. (On Yin Mountain, the wailing of ghosts will not stop either.)

Current Affairs Research

The Crisis Surrounding North China

— Fei Li

Since the establishment of the [Tanggu Truce Agreement] around June of last year, the extremely precarious situation in North China has gradually eased, and China and Japan have achieved a temporary so-called mutual understanding. As a result, our compatriots across the country no longer paid close attention to North China, which was constantly coveted by Japanese imperialism, assuming that the Great Wall would serve as a barrier, and they could live in peace and tranquility from then on. However, the facts tell us otherwise!

Now, we don't even need to delve into the history of the past few months. Just a summary of the recent events in North China and the talks given by central leaders after inspecting North China will reveal the following alarming issues:

Japanese and Korean Ronin Activities in Qinhuangdao. (Shen Bao Tianjin Electric Dispatch, March 27)

Japanese Troops Conduct Household Registration Survey in Zunhua. (Da Mei Evening News Beiping Electric Dispatch, March 30)

Yin Rugeng Discusses Indefinite Takeover of Malanyu. (Shen Bao Beiping Electric Dispatch, March 30)

Yan Huiqing's Remarks to Reporters Upon Arrival in Shanghai: [I am going to Pingjin this time to handle personal affairs and inspect the situation in North China along the way. I deeply feel the urgency of the situation in North China and hope that the entire nation will pay attention.] (Da Mei Evening News, March 30)

Japanese Troops and Garrisons Conduct Live-Fire Field Exercises in Tangshan, Luan County, Changli, Xifengkou, and Malanyu. (Shen Bao Beiping Electric Dispatch, March 31)

Heavy Japanese Troops and Numerous Aircraft Stationed in Malanyu Town Area; Airfield Under Construction. (Shen Bao Nanjing Electric Dispatch, April 1)

Japanese and Puppet Troops Reinforce Malanyu. (Da Mei Evening News Tianjin Electric Dispatch, April 1)

Japanese Sell Opium, Morphine, and Other Narcotics in the East. (Shen Bao Beiping Electric Dispatch, April 1)

Central Committee Member Zhang Ji's Remarks to Reporters Upon Returning to Nanjing After Inspecting North China: [North China is fraught with crises, and Beiping is in imminent danger of collapse, similar to the situation on the eve of the September 18th Incident in the Northeast. The day we become slaves is truly at hand.] (Shen Bao Nanjing Electric Dispatch)

Main Force of Japanese Troops Concentrated in Western Rehe. || Author's Note: Da Wan Bao reported on March 29 that approximately 13,000 Japanese troops are stationed at various passes along the Great Wall in Rehe Province. || (Shen Bao Beiping Special Electric Dispatch, April 2)

South Manchuria Railway East Asia Economic Research Association Sends Specialists to Investigate the Economic Situation in North China and Plans to Establish Special Agencies in Beiping, Tianjin, Qingdao, Jinan, Taiyuan, and Other Places to Develop Its Resources. (Shen Bao Hualian Electric Dispatch, April 2)

Yuguan Telegraph Bureau Still Controlled by Japanese Troops. (Shen Bao Tianjin Electric Dispatch)

Japanese Aircraft Threaten Fengrun County. (Da Wan Bao Tianjin Electric Dispatch, April 3)

[Japanese Troops in Gubeikou Reinforced by 400 Recently. Furthermore, in the past two days, two batches of Japanese troops passed through Gu to inspect the border of Chahar. The Japanese are currently rushing to repair the motor roads at Baimaguan and other passes.] (Da Wan Bao Beiping Electric Dispatch, April 3)

Japanese Puppets Actively Constructing Railways (between Pingquan and Chifeng, between Lingyuan and Lengkou, etc.) and Military Motor Roads (between Chaoyang and Chifeng, between Chifeng and Chengde, etc.) in Rehe Province and Along the Great Wall. || (Shen Bao Changchun Correspondence, April 3)

Analyzing the above phenomena, it is very clear to recognize how Japanese imperialists are using the following methods to advance into North China: 1. Military Occupation; 2. Utilizing Traitors and Japanese-Korean Ronin to Create Trouble; 3. Dispatching Personnel to Conduct Inspections in the Interior; 4. Selling Narcotics to Harm the Chinese. As a result, our vast territory of North China and tens of millions of people are becoming increasingly endangered under these four vicious policies of aggression.

[North China is Extremely Endangered!] A few people have shouted this weak cry, but after all, this cry is somewhat weak, and it has not yet shaken the eardrums of the vast Chinese populace and awakened their attention. On the other hand, there is still no news of the government's attitude and countermeasures. It is only heard that Huang Fu is going south, [actually bearing the nature of contacting the highest authorities in Beijing regarding certain important diplomatic matters.] This is indeed difficult to understand.

A Tokyo electric dispatch on April 4 stated: [Japan has no intention of invading China. This can be determined by observing the recent attitude of the Kwantung Army. The key to our country lies in correctly understanding the current situation in North China, seeking to improve the prosperity of the people, and not spreading rumors that shake people's hearts (Author's note: Referring to the talks given by Central Committee Member Zhang Ji after inspecting North China) to the outside world.] It is hoped that the gentlemen of the Party-state will not be misled by this hypocritical defense of Japanese imperialism, and it is also hoped that the people of the whole country will not be misled by it. It is necessary to closely safeguard North China |and even the whole country|. If, in the event of an unforeseen catastrophe, war descends upon North China again, then it is hoped that the people of the whole country will quickly unite and launch a small, elite resistance for the sake of the survival of the Chinese people!

There are also clerks in the warehouse - [Warehouse Gentlemen].

Heh heh! Should there also be such a nice-sounding name? Isn't it the same suffering, having to squeeze in and out of the cargo piles with everyone, overturning boxes and barrels: climbing to the top of the piles, climbing into the corners of the walls, in narrow crevices, in dark tunnels, bending over, using flashlights to shine on the Mark···No···Weight··· on each piece of cargo, shouting with straightened throats, letting the staff of the big merchants record it.

Sometimes, the forehead bumps into the corner of a box, the arms and legs are torn by nails, bleeding. There's nothing to stop the bleeding in the warehouse, grab a handful of dust from the corner of the door, pull a spider web and apply it, that's a good method.

In the hot weather, there is no air conditioning, no fans in the warehouse. Clerks and laborers are shirtless, sweating one layer and covered with a layer of dust and sand, panting and panting in the moldy smell. In the cold weather, there is no water heater in the warehouse. Cold air rises from the cement floor. The clerks shrink their bodies and shiver as much as possible. When they can't stand the cold, they jump around. But the laborers can still endure it. They are often pressed into a sweat by cargo weighing thousands of pounds.

A Brief Discussion on the Question of [Which Came First, the Chicken or the Egg?]

— Ke Shi

After reading Mr. Chi Fo's [The Broad Meaning of Which Came First, the Chicken or the Egg?] in the 67th issue of the Amateur Weekly, I also feel that I have a few words to say.

This question seems simple on the surface, but it is actually very complicated. It has been discussed as a central problem in genetics. What must first be understood in genetics is: Does the body originate from the germ plasm, or does the germ plasm originate from the body? On this, the ancients spent a lot of thought and established several hypotheses, but the important ones are roughly the following two schools:

(1) Argues that [the egg is produced by the chicken]. Darwin can be taken as the representative of this school. Darwin once established a hypothesis, assuming that each cell of an animal's body can emit a kind of ultramicroscopic microparticle, called [gemmules]. It is said that these gemmules enter the blood and are carried by it to the germ cells, where they are stored. Later, the germ cells develop into new individuals, so they resemble the parent body.

(2) Argues that [the chicken is produced by the egg]. Weismann can be taken as the representative of this school. Weismann once established a theory,

explaining that the germ plasm of germ cells is transmitted from the germ plasm of previous generations, and is not produced by the individual. Therefore, the germ plasm is inherited from one generation to the next, while the cells of the body are produced by the germ plasm. He constructed his [theory of germ plasm continuity] in this way.

These two schools of thought are not only very important in genetics, but also extremely important in the theory of variation and evolution. If we follow Darwin's hypothesis, if the individual is affected by the environment in his life and an effect occurs, it can also be transmitted to the germ plasm and cause variations in future generations. If we follow Weismann's theory, only if the germ plasm itself undergoes variation can it be transmitted to future generations. The influence of the individual's environment cannot reach the germ plasm. Finally, because science values proof, Darwin's gemmules could not be proven, but Weismann's theory found some evidence under the microscope. Therefore, many biologists supported Weismann's theory. Mr. Chi Fo's argument that the egg came before the chicken can perhaps be said to belong to the Weismann school of thought.

However, if we analyze and observe, and then look at it comprehensively, although many hereditary traits seem to be directly inheritable: some new species of variation seem to be able to arise independently - because the reasons are unknown, it seems that they are discovered in offspring due to variations in the germ plasm. But from another perspective, there are indeed many examples of organisms undergoing variation and evolution due to the influence of the living environment. For example, the evolutionary explanation of the origin of mankind is: first there were ape-like creatures living in trees: they learned to sit and stand upright from this lifestyle. And they freed their hands, which they could use to climb branches and pick fruits. When the forests declined, they descended to the ground. Then, they were able to walk on two feet with difficulty, and also learned to grasp wooden sticks and use tools with their hands. The upright posture and the new environment helped to develop the brain, and the development of the brain also helped to develop work skills. From these examples, it can be seen that variation and evolution are actually related to the individual's living conditions. It is difficult to explain by simply attributing it to changes in the germ plasm. Therefore, we can very well say that the life of the chicken can affect the egg, and the egg transmits this influence to the chicken. In recent years, Conklin proposed that modern biologists have a tendency to view organisms as a whole; Thomson further explained that organisms should be observed in conjunction with the environment. Perhaps this is due to these facts?

Now, let's put aside empty talk and talk about the topic itself again. Mr. Chi Fo believes that there must be an egg before there is a chicken. This is certainly one opinion of biologists, but it is a very serious mistake to cite Dr. Luo Guangting's [theory of spontaneous generation] as proof. It is not necessary for me to say more about the unreliability of Dr. Luo's words. Just read the letters from Hartman of Lingnan University and Hoarepoeue of the Pasteur Institute (Continental Magazine, Volume 2, Issue 5), and the discussions of several domestic scientists, and you will know. As for words such as [a sparrow entering the sea becomes a clam] and [a sheep can be planted], they are not only not commonplace, but also not common sense. They are just like what Hao Yixing said: [The ancients were not precise in observing things and made reckless measurements.] It would be extremely terrible if someone still believed it today.

Commentary

Marriage and the Nation

— Han Ying

As long as we are willing to pay attention to social trivia, we can often discover some facts that are closely related to social problems. About ten days ago, under the headline [Marriage Failed After Two Years], we saw another such episode: Sun Xiu'e and Sun Yusheng have been married for more than two years. Although they live in the same room, they have never had sexual intercourse. Recently, they hired a lawyer to sue Sun Yusheng for being born impotent and requested a divorce. Sun Yusheng claimed that he stopped having sex due to lung disease and did not have any hidden illness. He also hired a lawyer to apply for mediation.

Marriage and health are very closely related. The union of men and women is a natural instinct: unless there is some physical defect, everyone has this need. But a person must also have a certain condition for marriage; lacking this condition, he has no qualification for marriage. This has long been stipulated in the marriage laws of various European and American countries. When a person wants to marry, he must undergo an examination by a doctor to prove that his body has reached maturity and has no defects. Only then will the state allow marriage; conversely, if the body is not fully developed or has incurable diseases, he will not be granted the right to marry. This is certainly a loss for a small number of people, but it is very beneficial to the majority. This not only relates to the happiness of individuals or families; its influence on the country, the nation, and even all mankind is also very significant.

But it is not so in our country. It is very free and convenient for people in our country to marry. Whether it is a man or a woman, as long as they are willing to marry themselves, or their parents want them to marry, they can implement it immediately. As for whether the age has reached adulthood, whether the body development is complete, or whether they have infectious diseases, hereditary diseases or hidden illnesses, they can ignore everything. Not only do they ignore it themselves, but the country does not interfere. Therefore, the marriage situation in our country has all kinds of strange phenomena. [The command of the parents and the words of the matchmaker] are always the most compliant with the rules; betrothal from the womb or child brides have almost become customs. They do not care at all about the health status of both men and women, whether it has reached or can reach a level and qualification for marriage, adhering to the [marriage for the sake of marriage] purpose. Small couples of thirteen or fourteen years old can create small citizens, and it is spread in all directions as a good story: bedridden, even dying, with a body temperature about to dissipate, the parents sometimes have to find a bride for him to cheer him up, hoping that he can be brought back to life. Some men with sexually transmitted diseases marry because they superstitiously believe that intercourse with a virgin can relieve their pain. Hereditary diseases are even more latent and difficult to see. Even if they can be inherited, that is a matter for later generations, and it cannot be used as an obstacle to our marriage. Not only is old-style marriage like this, but isn't free love marriage the same? Some of them are immersed in temporary enthusiasm, so they can't take care of anything else; some are lured by money or beauty, what does health matter? In short, marriage in our country is too free and too casual. The union of Sun Xiu'e and Sun Yusheng is not considered how unique.

In our view, health is not only related to marriage, but health is even the most important condition among all marriage conditions. It must be known that the union of the two sexes, in addition to mutual assistance and satisfying sexual life, also bears a mission of reproducing the race. The so-called reproduction of the race is not just about giving birth to children and passing on grandchildren. Attention should also be paid to the improvement of the race, so that one's own race can develop upward. This is the teaching that modern eugenics gives us. Therefore, a person should wait until his body has matured and has no defects before he can implement marriage; if he does not have a qualification for marriage, trying it rashly will not only fail to bring happiness to himself, but also leave harm to the race. For the sake of personal and family happiness, for the sake of the future of the society, the country, and the nation, people in our country should change their always hasty attitude toward marriage and pay close attention to the health conditions of both men and women. As for the government, it should not ignore this issue. On the one hand, in education, it can use educational tools to vigorously carry out effective propaganda, so that marriage knowledge and eugenics can be fully popularized among the people; on the other hand, in law, there should be a regulation restricting marriage, so that the people dare not regard marriage as child's play. Then, the unfortunate events that occur in the future regarding marriage may be reduced as a result; this is not without some benefit to the development of the country and the nation!

Vocational Education Now and in the Future

— Ji Xin

[The most urgent need for Chinese education at present is to strive to develop vocational education.] This is what International Labour Office Deputy Director Maurette contributed to the Ministry of Education.

Vocational education, the name itself has many problems. But I don't want to discuss this aspect. I just want to analyze the educational situation indicated by the word vocational: what path is it taking? What impact does it have on society? And its future trends.

(1) Vocational Education and Commercial Education! If vocational education is done successfully, it is commercial education, and it can be regarded as a darling of the times. Universities have business schools or business departments, senior high schools have business departments, some normal schools have attached vocational classes in business, and there are even independent business schools. In terms of students' future prospects, it is often better than students in other departments, and even better than graduates of normal schools. This phenomenon, like the banking industry in recent years, is a deformed development. The future prospects of business students are good, and the development of banks and other similar businesses makes the city appear prosperous, but the countryside has been depleted and has become a huge belly. This is not a gratifying phenomenon, but a tragic harbinger. They are not direct producers. In China today, they are an unnecessary consumption. The more developed this type of consumption-oriented vocational education, the weaker the financial resources for other occupations will become. If the talents trained by schools and social undertakings show a phenomenon of oversupply, then it is equivalent to ordinary schools, only creating high-level vagrants and an army of unemployed reserves. Even if supply and demand can match, it is equal to digging one's own grave.

(2) Vocational Education and Light Industry｜In schools at all levels, vocational education has everything. Engineering, agriculture, business, and even independent vocational schools. Universities are not to be mentioned, but as for secondary vocational schools, most of them offer textile, dyeing, banking, accounting, crafts and other departments. Although there are also departments related to mechanical industry, agriculture, etc., it is rare to find ones that match the name and reality and have some achievements. Therefore, the development of secondary vocational education can at best provide some help in the field of light industry. In China today, light industry has two fates: first, the development of light industry is impossible. In the current stage of world economic panic, the dumping policies of capitalist countries have swallowed the entire colonial market, and even our last drop of blood will be sucked away. What can be done in countries without tariff protection? Second, light industry is not needed. A country that is so backward and fragmented needs a lot of construction and the manufacture of a large number of means of production. In this difficult transitional era, small light industry is of no help and is not needed. Clearly speaking, light industry is a manufacturing of consumer goods.

In this way, vocational education in China has not created much welfare. The biggest reasons are two: first, the deformed development of the capital economy has made commercial education occupy an important position in vocational education. Second, because of the copying of the education system, vocational subjects far from reality are opened in the same way as drawing a gourd. We still need vocational education, but the future direction must be re-opened.

What kind of vocational education is needed, this issue has a wide scope. Here, only one trend can be proposed. That is, what we need in the future is productive vocational education.

Productive vocational education has two characteristics:

(1) Under the current situation, it is necessary to exclude consumption-oriented vocational education, to enable everyone to directly participate in production, and to build a new type of country.

(2) Develop heavy industry, use China's natural wealth, mechanize various industries and agriculture, and even require their electrification.

Productive vocational education is for society, not for individuals, for the needs of the majority, not for the enjoyment of the minority.

International Wireless Broadcasting Station

Bees in the Soviet Second Five-Year Plan

— Pei Ren

Spring has come, and all living things are busy moving around. Bees are one of them. They are a very organized, highly collective animal, which is an animal that everyone is very interested in.

Beekeeping is a very common job in the Soviet Union. From a small and unimportant fragment of the rural economy, bee culture has now become an important department, which is scientifically planned and placed under central management.

In 1929-30, the Soviet Union had already begun to use beehive frames to replace the old wooden box houses for the protection of bees. In 1919, only 17% of the suitable beehives remained on the beehive frames, but in 1926 the percentage was increased to 54.9, and in 1931 it was increased to 61.7. This great progress came with the collectivization of the countryside, and now it has greatly increased. The Soviet Union has put it on a large production basis, and has a special management agency.

According to statistics, the total number of beehives in the entire Soviet Union was 4,466,200 as of January 1, 1931, of which 2,755,100 were on beehive frames. By January 1, 1932, 1,500,000 had been added in collective farms, and 50,000 had been added in state farms.

Beekeeping is being tested everywhere in the Soviet Union, especially in the North Caucasus, Siberia, the Far East, Bashkiria, Ukraine, and the Central Black Soil Belt and other important areas.

One of the important tasks of the Second Five-Year Plan is to increase the harvest of agricultural products. As an important medium for plant pollination, bees play a decisive role in this task. For this purpose, the Agricultural Committee decided to increase the work of beekeeping in state farms. Because not only can great benefits be obtained for agricultural crops, beekeeping can also obtain honey and wax, which greatly increases the supply of human food.

We accidentally hear the buzzing sound of bees this spring, but have we ever thought about what great relationship they have with us humans?

Book and Newspaper Reviews

Adult Learning

— Chen Jiyun

｜Translated by Du Zuo and Zhu Junyi, published by the Commercial Press, priced at two yuan and six jiao｜

Of our 400 million compatriots, approximately 80% are adults who have not received education, totaling about 320 million. Many of these compatriots believe that learning is easier during childhood and adolescence. They think that adults have diminished pure curiosity, fixed neural pathways, and lost assimilation abilities, making it very difficult to learn new concepts. This traditional thinking is enough to discourage many illiterate adults and hinder their boundless progress. In fact, according to the results of various experiments by Thorndike and others on adults learning different tasks, such views are completely wrong. He believed that the energy for learning never stops, that adults remain highly adaptable or teachable, and that they can continue to learn after the age of twenty-five. This book reports on the changes in the quantity and nature of learning ability from the ages of fifteen to forty-five, especially from twenty-five to forty-five, as well as the introduction of various learning methods.

The book is divided into thirteen chapters. The first chapter is an introduction, the second chapter reports on the facts of adult learning as reported by general psychology and education, the third chapter compares adult learning with children's learning, the fourth chapter discusses the learning of intelligent adults, the fifth chapter discusses the learning of low-ability adults, the sixth chapter discusses the learning of adults in secretarial schools, the seventh chapter discusses adult learning of secondary school subjects in public night schools, the eighth chapter is supplementary experiments, the ninth chapter is on the difference between completely new learning and age, the tenth chapter is on evidence regarding adult learning, the eleventh chapter is on the reasons for the change in learning ability and the amount learned due to age, the twelfth chapter is on the qualitative differences between age and learning, and the thirteenth chapter is on practical applications. There are also several pages of appendices.

The language of the book is simple and fresh, the translation is fluent, and it is well worth reading. It is hoped that the 320 million uneducated compatriots should not consider themselves too old, nor should they be unduly fearful and suppress their learning. They should no longer use this fear as an excuse to abandon what they should be learning. Even educated compatriots should continue their efforts, because our energy for learning continues unabated and never stops. Today, knowledge advances by leaps and bounds. What we learned from the ages of ten to twenty becomes obsolete by the time we are forty. If we continue to do things according to old methods, we will inevitably stumble and face constant danger. For example, when driving a car or turning on and off ordinary lights, they will not know what to do. Furthermore, regarding basic hygiene and prevention, they will endanger their lives due to negligence. Therefore, if we want the progress of literature, art, and science to be boundless, there is no other way than continuing education inside and outside of schools. It is hoped that adults will pay attention to this.

Monograph

Roosevelt's Achievements in the First Year of Office

— Jian Fu

Franklin D. Roosevelt, the thirty-second President of the United States, was sworn into office on March 4th of last year. By now, it has been a full year. In this year, some have praised him, and some have criticized him. But what are his achievements? We have no choice but to analyze them from an objective standpoint. Here, due to space limitations, we will only discuss the economic aspects.

The day Roosevelt took office was when the financial crisis in the United States was at its worst. On that day, the banks in all forty-eight states of the United States were in a state of great panic. If it were a president with weak abilities, he would surely be flustered and at a loss in the face of such a serious blow. However, Roosevelt was able to resolutely resolve the matter step by step. The day after taking office, he announced that all banks in the country would be closed for ten days. A day later, he ordered a ban on the export of gold and silver. On the seventh day, the Ministry of Finance issued new banking regulations. Thus, this unprecedented storm was calmed.

With the financial crisis resolved, Roosevelt then moved to rescue rural areas and relieve unemployment. At the same time, he stood on the position of international coordination and discussed international economic issues with representatives of various countries in preparation for the London World Economic Conference. Just as representatives from various countries were flocking to the United States, Roosevelt announced the abandonment of the gold standard and submitted an inflation bill to both houses of Congress. Although this did not disrupt the Washington Talks, it sowed the seeds for the bankruptcy of the World Economic Conference.

As expected, the World Economic Conference held in June ultimately broke down due to the lack of results on the issue of stabilizing exchange rates. After the conference, international economic problems not only did not improve, but also led to the (economic self-sufficiency) of various countries. This economic self-sufficiency was fully expressed in the United States by the Industrial Recovery Act | namely, the Blue Eagle Movement |. Although the banner of the Industrial Recovery Act still had important text transferred to page 5

Page 20

Page 21

The banner called for [increasing wages and providing workers with methods to obtain work, in order to stabilize industry and cope with the rapid changes of the past two years]. However, today, the facts have proven that this is just a pipe dream. The industrial production index did temporarily increase in June and July, when the Industrial Recovery Act was first implemented. However, in August, the tragic situation returned. After that, it declined almost month by month. Originally, although the Industrial Recovery Act stipulated increasing wages and reducing working hours, in reality, (1) real wages could not keep up with nominal wages, and (2) reducing working hours only reduced the hours of employed workers and distributed them to some unemployed workers, sacrificing the former to supply the latter. Therefore, although this act sounds so appealing, it did not increase the purchasing power and consumption power of workers at all.

Witnessing the return of this tragic scene, Roosevelt quickly implemented a gold purchase policy on October 25 before things completely failed. Why buy gold? This has a dual meaning. On the one hand, because domestic opposition to the monetary inflation policy was growing, the government had to use gold purchases to indicate the stabilization of the currency value (the so-called devaluation of the currency to 59.06 cents is one such indication); on the other hand, the fall in the external exchange rate of the US dollar could stimulate the increase in exports. Gold has already been purchased in large quantities, followed by a tight measure to raise the price of silver and purchase silver. The former is a method of attacking gold standard countries to assist one's own trade; while the latter is a policy of increasing industrial recovery at the expense of silver standard countries (China).

Looking at the economic policies adopted by Roosevelt in his first year in office, we can say with certainty that he is completely standing on the viewpoint of monetary inflation to deal with the disaster of the American economic panic. The effect of monetary inflation is temporary, so Roosevelt's relief of the panic is also temporary. Roosevelt is a political leader with considerable abilities, but even if his abilities were doubled, facing this economic crisis full of contradictions, I am afraid he would end up sighing in vain!

A Big Girl Receives an Award in the Midst of Children's Day Celebrations

— Ms. Shen Airong

Because I was receiving an award for the Women's National Products Year essay contest, I didn't have an admission ticket. A big girl like me also had to participate in the Children's Day celebration. "The award ceremony is on the third floor," they said to me after knowing my background.

The rubber soles of my basketball shoes kissed all three floors of the stairs. Three fellow award recipients from Songjiang Girls' High School had arrived before me, wandering aimlessly on the third floor. After being guided by a receptionist, they finally learned that the essay award ceremony was being held in the hall on the second floor.

Running to the second floor, a burst of noisy and chaotic voices came from the dark, crowded heads in front of the stage, suppressing and raising the sharp voice of the lady speaking on the stage.

It's Children's Day! In front of the stage were innocent faces holding gifts and smiling. They probably weren't interested in the speech, right? They were just constantly restless, disrupting the order of the venue.

A round of applause sent the lady down and welcomed the man. His mouth opened like a goldfish breathing, and not a single word could be heard. The noise drowned out the voice. Another round of applause led to a Miss Beiping, speaking in a crisp Northern accent, leading a child to introduce him to the audience: "This is Mr. Cai Yuanpei's son, Mr. Cai XX. He is very smart. Today, we have invited him to give a speech." The lights on both sides shone on his little face, making him look even more adorable. However, he just opened his mouth, bowed, and retreated, probably a little shy, right? There were also two children with red clothes and apple-shaped faces, the daughters of Mr. Pan Yangyao, who served as the mayor of the National Products Company Children's Market, the important people of the Children's Market! The photographer was very busy.

Miss Beiping announced the proposals: 1. Relief for street children; 2. Establishment of nurseries; 3. ... The applause ended this report.

The essay award ceremony began. Mr. Nie Zengjifen and Mr. Pan Yangyao presented the awards. There were sixty-two winners from the university and high school divisions. Because of the lack of time, only the top five were awarded at the time. The remaining winners were invited to the backstage. Sixth, yes, I remember I was sixth, so I went to the backstage and received a red envelope that looked like an invitation. The five words "Ms. Shen Airong" were neatly written in the middle.

The entertainment began. The first program was a singing performance by the Shanghai Guangci Hospital Boy Scouts. What heroic children, what agile and neat movements! Who says China is a sick man of Asia? But, how great it would be if all the children in the country had this strong physique and enterprising spirit. Otherwise, local development will not be very effective.

It was already four o'clock. Although there were still many wonderful programs to come, I had a little matter to attend to, so I had to say goodbye to these many adorable children and this children's land, and left the gate of the Lakeside Society.

Amateur Entertainment

Throwing an Egg into a Bottle

— Yingqiu

This game can be used as an experiment in physics for [thermal expansion and contraction]. Readers, if you have free time, you may want to try it.

Buy a chicken egg or duck egg, immerse it in a pot of hot water to make the egg white slightly harden, and then remove the shell. On the other hand, take a small-necked bottle, the mouth of which must be slightly smaller than the egg, and then take a few pieces of paper, light them on fire, and throw them into the bottle. The air in the bottle expands due to heat, and a part of it escapes from the mouth of the bottle. While the fire is still burning, place the shelled egg at the mouth of the bottle. The air in the bottle is thin, and the pressure of the outside air presses against the mouth of the bottle. When the fire goes out, the air in the bottle cools and shrinks in volume. The outside air has no choice but to enter the bottle, but because the egg is blocking it, the air outside the bottle presses on the egg, and the air inside the bottle is weak. The egg has no choice but to fall into the bottle with a bang.

Before playing, we should find a bottle with a small neck and a large bottom, because the volume of the bottle is larger, the volume of air in the bottle can also be larger, and it will be easier to do.

Amateur Cafe

No Way Out

— Jianshe

I am a person in the ranks of the petty bourgeoisie. Although that's what I say, life is urgently threatening me. From my family environment, I have to solve my life problems, but life problems are so difficult to solve. What should I do?

I want to find a reliable and legitimate job no matter what. But finding a job is so difficult and unfamiliar. I now feel like I am walking in a deep forest. How can I find my way out?

Some people always agree with me becoming a teacher. I have also worked as a teacher. I feel that if there is no other better path, this is also a good path. Because the life of a teacher is often close to books. Being able to constantly wash myself in knowledge, I will surely be able to obtain many opportunities for tempering and benefits from this washing. But how can I find a satisfactory teaching position? The educational circles everywhere are full of factions. Those who are in their faction can get in, but those who are not in their faction will be excluded by any means. Moreover, general principals are the least trusting of us young people. They all think that the old are good, their knowledge is profound, and their experience is rich, while young people are all useless waste. Even if they have some knowledge, it is only superficial. And it is fundamentally dangerous, maybe they will carry out some kind of [sex] propaganda in the first class. So, they feel a headache as soon as they see us young people. How can we gain their trust in this way?

It is difficult to become a teacher, so some people advise me to enter politics. Although I am unwilling to engage in political activities, I cannot say anything for the sake of life problems. So I thought about it too. But the political world is even more a matter of powerful families and personal connections. The first point is that factions are very strict. Under the big faction, there are small factions. Within the small faction, there are those who are the most trusted and those who are the next most trusted. If you did not have a close relationship with them in the first place, then even if you sell yourself and seek refuge, you will not be able to join that organization. The second point is that even for the smallest clerk, a big figure must recommend him. Without a big figure to speak for you, you cannot even find a doorman.

So some people want me to join the military. They say that this is quite suitable for me. Because in there, as long as you endure hardship and are willing to give up your life, you will have a chance to stand out. Standing out is indeed needed, but who is this life given to? I am very hesitant. And the threat of life is so terrible. But this is also a useless attempt! The military is the same as the political world. Powerful families are very strict. Without a close and long-term connection with them, you cannot get in no matter what.

So, according to the general saying, the paths that intellectuals can take are all blocked. Because I have no commercial knowledge, I naturally cannot get into commercial organizations. Born without literary genius, I cannot beg for food from bookstores and magazines and newspapers. But my life problems always have to be solved! But how should I solve them?

Lost Peace of Mind

— Jianshe

I have recently gradually developed a feeling of ____. I have learned that life is so alienated and cold, so I am becoming tired of life. At first, when I suffered from this ____, I could still maintain my daily routine. Now, this attack has become deeper and heavier, causing me to gradually abandon the rules of daily life. I feel that everything is gloomy, and I am becoming tired of everything.

In the past, I felt that philosophy was the most approachable. I was very willing to wander in the labyrinth of philosophy day and night, allowing those profound maxims to deeply intoxicate me. I remember there was a time when I desperately read Nietzsche. I felt that he was an incredible hero, and his powerful words of the Superman theory seemed like an alarm bell to awaken the world. Later, I read Hegel, and I also felt that he was a great man who surpassed the past and the present. I lingered between his theories of the state, and I felt that the soul of Germany was grasped by him. Then I became tired, and I unreasonably gave them up. I never read them again. Why is this? I can't say clearly. I only feel that my heart can no longer be so stable, no longer stably following the writing of these great philosophers, and being introduced into their profound mysteries. Not only that, I simply get upset when I see them.

Following this, I started reading novels like a madman. I read an unusually large number of novels. I often wanted to finish a story so much that I forgot to eat and forgot to sleep. I sympathized greatly with the heroine. I felt that a girl who won a love was as if I was also participating in that victory. Sometimes, when a story ended tragically, I felt like I had received a blow to my heart, and I was overwhelmed with sadness. From classical, romantic, to various new works now. For a while, my mind was full of yearnings for various stories: and many times I seemed to be living in that novel, I forgot all the circumstances of this reality. At that time, I was secretly and uncontrollably pleased. Because although I lost my interest in philosophy, I have now gained a new home. But now! : : : I don't want to read any novels. I no longer feel that the sweet story can tempt me: I no longer feel that the situation is worth my lingering. My mind is extraordinarily gloomy. I feel that all efforts are meaningless.

During this time, I also asked myself whether I had lost my health, and whether the weakness of my body was affecting my mood? But my body is still strong, it will not affect my mood, only my mood affects it. So I became upset. I can't find the reason for this upset, I'm just upset. I also feel that everything is empty, everything is indifferent, the world will not understand me, and I am too lazy to understand others. Life is only prolonged in a dying state. I am extremely decadent.

Where am I going? Can I still find my peace of mind? Alas, how panicked I am! How painful I am!

Biography of a Celebrity

Marconi, Inventor of Wireless Radio (1)

— Sen Ran

Among all the great inventions of modern times, wireless radio occupies a very important position. If the emergence of trains, ships, and airplanes shortened the distance of space, then, because of the invention of wireless radio, the distance of space has been completely broken down. With wireless radio, we can sit in Shanghai and hear the speeches of politicians in London and the songs of girls in New York; with wireless radio, generals can sit at home and command millions of land, sea, and air forces, and speculators can sit in Shanghai and know the situation of the New York Stock Exchange. If you are happy, you can stay in Shanghai and ask a photography studio in Berlin to take an artistic photo of you, and you can also use wireless radio to achieve your goal. The invention of wireless radio has brought together the mainland, the ocean, and the space, in short, the entire space. From this, commerce, military affairs, politics, and even the entire life of mankind have gained great convenience.

But who exactly is the inventor of wireless radio? This is Marconi (Guglielmo Marconi) we are going to talk about.

Marconi was born on April 25, 1874, in the village of Griffen near Bologna, Italy. His father was an Italian landowner, and his mother came from a distinguished Irish family. Therefore, he lived a very comfortable life from an early age, and poverty and suffering had little to do with him.

Because of his good family environment, Marconi's education was naturally solved according to his wishes. At the age of fifteen, he entered the University of Bologna, where he was often guided by Augusto Righi, a famous physicist in Italy at the time.

Marconi was certainly a gifted person. He was very diligent since he was a child, and he had a special love for natural science. When he was still a twelve-year-old boy, Dr. Heinrich Hertz had already begun his famous experiment, which undoubtedly had a great influence on the clever Marconi who especially loved natural science. After reading Hertz's experimental report, he immediately had a feeling: it is possible to communicate without electric wires!

Hertz's experiment increased Marconi's interest in electrical research. At the same time, Professor Righi was also working hard on the research of [Hertzian waves], which undoubtedly had an even greater relationship with Marconi. Because of his intelligence, diligence, and love of electrical research, Professor Righi also liked him very much. He not only received many valuable lessons from this famous physics professor, but also received many practical benefits. In guiding Marconi's research, Professor Righi lent him all his wireless equipment, such as arc generators, etc., and encouraged him to work hard on the invention of wireless radio. As a result, Marconi made up his mind to study wireless radio. At this time, he was still a twenty-two-year-old youth.

Initially, he began experimenting in the yard of his hometown. He first erected a bamboo pole in one corner, and then erected another bamboo pole in another corner, and then connected what is today called a Radiator (wireless radio transmission and reception line) to the poles erected in these two corners, and then hung a Blik can at the upper end of the Radiator to work hard on his work. This method, in the eyes of the villagers, was of course very strange and laughable. However, Marconi did not pay any attention to people's ridicule, but just worked hard to do his [wonderful] things. In this way, day after day, Marconi achieved his first success. If he hung the Blik can about six feet above the ground, he could transmit signals a distance of 100 yards; if he raised the Blik can to 14 feet, he could transmit signals a distance of about 300 yards. As a result, he experimented and found that if he increased the amount (electrical capacity) of the Blik can and its height of suspension, he could achieve communication of 1.5 miles.

Marconi once asked the following question in Righi's laboratory: How to increase the sensing distance of electric waves? Righi's answer to this question was: [Raise your vibrator and see]. This was a great inspiration for Marconi's research. His initial success was achieved under this inspiration, in his efforts to study the relationship between the height of the Radiator and the communication distance.

In order to widely publish the results of his research, Marconi wrote a letter to Sir W.H. Preece, the chief engineer of the British Post Office at the time.

At that time, Preece was also researching his wireless telegraph, and he had made considerable achievements. But after reading Marconi's research, he felt that this Italian youth was even more brilliant than himself. He immediately wrote a very detailed reply to discuss the issue of wireless radio with Marconi, and at the same time wrote the following words at the end of the letter: [......If it does not hinder you, then please come to England no matter what. Regarding your invention, we will seek as many conveniences as possible.] (To be continued)
